The Eternal Attributes: Definitions and Distinctions
Author enumerates eternal attributes and defines them with a key clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of God's eternal attributes (knowledge, power, life, strength, hearing, sight, and will) and the distinction between the eternity of attributes and the temporality of their objects.

Core Idea
God's attributes are eternal; their objects are not.

In this passage, the author enumerates the eternal attributes of God and provides concise definitions for each. He also clarifies a common confusion: the eternity of attributes like hearing does not mean their objects (sounds and sights) are eternal. This lesson presents the foundational definitions for understanding divine attributes in the Maturidi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of attributes
Begin by reading the list of ten attributes: knowledge, power, life, strength, hearing, sight, will, action/creation, providing sustenance, and speech. Notice that some are defined later and some are synonymous.
The list includes 'al-quwwa' (strength) which is clarified as synonymous with power.
2
Understand each definition
Focus on the definitions of knowledge, power, life, strength, hearing, and sight. Each defines an eternal attribute with a specific function: knowledge discloses, power influences, life validates, strength is power, hearing relates to sounds, sight relates to sights.
The definition of hearing and sight emphasizes divine perception without physical organs.
3
Analyze the clarification about eternity
Read the paragraph that explains why the eternity of hearing and sight does not imply the eternity of sounds and sights. This is a key theological point: attributes are eternal, but their relations (ta‘alluqāt) to created things occur in time.
Compare with knowledge and power: known things and objects of power are created, yet knowledge and power are eternal.
4
Note the incomplete definition of will
The passage begins defining will and intention but cuts off. Understand that will is an attribute that specifies which possibility occurs at a given time, but the full definition is missing. This may be continued in the next lesson.

His eternal attributes (ṣifātuhu ta‘ālā al-azaliyya)
Knowledge - Power - Life - Strength - Hearing - Sight - Will and Intention - Action and Creation - Providing Sustenance - Speech
And they are, i.e., His eternal attributes.
Knowledge: It is an eternal attribute by which the known things (ma‘lūmāt) are disclosed when it is related (ta‘alluq) to them.
Power: It is an eternal attribute that influences the objects of power (maqdūrāt) when it is related to them.
Life: It is an eternal attribute that necessitates the validity of knowledge.
Strength: It is in the meaning of power from other than Saari [؟].
Hearing: It is an attribute that relates to sounds (masmū‘āt).
Sight: It is an attribute that relates to sights (mubṣirāt), so it perceives completely, not in the way of imagination (takhayyul) or illusion (tawahhum), nor in the way of the effect of a sense or the arrival of air.
And the eternity of the two does not necessitate the eternity of sounds and sights, just as the eternity of knowledge and power does not necessitate the eternity of known things and objects of power, because they are eternal attributes that have newly occurring relations (ta‘alluqāt) to events (ḥawādith).
And Will and Intention: They are two expressions for an attribute in the living being (ḥayy) that necessitates the specification of one of the two possibilities (maqdūrayn) at one of the times to occur, while the proportion of power (qudra) is equal to all, and that the relation of knowledge is subsequent to the occurrence.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of God's eternal attributes as defined in the Maturidi tradition. The author lists ten attributes: knowledge, power, life, strength (quwwa), hearing, sight, will, action, creation, providing sustenance, and speech. Then he defines each. Knowledge is an eternal attribute by which information is disclosed when it is related to them. Power is an eternal attribute that affects the objects of power when related. Life is an eternal attribute that necessitates the validity of knowledge. Strength is synonymous with power but from other than... (text unclear). Hearing is an attribute related to sounds. Sight is an attribute related to sights, perceiving completely without imagination or illusion or through the effect of a sense or air. He notes that the eternity of hearing and sight does not entail the eternity of sounds and sights, just as the eternity of knowledge and power does not entail the eternity of known things and objects of power, because they are eternal attributes that have newly occurring relations to events. Finally, Will and Intention are two expressions for an attribute in the living being that necessitates the specification of one of two possibilities at a given time to occur, while the ability (qudra) is equally related to all, and the relation of knowledge follows the occurrence.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are eternal, but they relate to temporal objects without becoming temporal themselves.

Eternal Attributes: List and Definitions
Taftazani lists the eternal attributes and defines knowledge, power, life, and strength.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the list of Allah's eternal attributes and the definitions of knowledge, power, life, and strength as given by Taftazani.

Core Idea
Allah's eternal attributes each have a specific function in relation to creation.

In this passage, Taftazani enumerates the eternal attributes of Allah and begins defining the first four. These definitions establish that knowledge discloses, power affects, life enables, and strength is synonymous with power. Understanding these foundational concepts is essential for grasping later discussions on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of attributes
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the attributes listed with hyphens: hearing, sight, will, action, etc.
The list includes 12 attributes, but only four are defined in this passage.
2
Understand 'eternal attributes'
The text says 'His eternal attributes'. Recognize that these are not temporary or created; they are inherent to Allah.
3
Examine the definition of knowledge and power
Knowledge discloses known things; power affects objects of power. Both occur 'when it relates to them' (at t'alluqi biha).
The phrase 'عند تعلقها بها' is crucial: the attributes' effect depends on relation to their objects.
4
Examine the definitions of life and strength
Life necessitates the soundness of knowledge, and strength is said to be synonymous with power. Note the unclear phrase 'من سوى سارى'.
Strength is often understood as a synonym for power in this context.

His eternal attributes. Knowledge - Power - Life - Strength - Hearing - Sight - Will and Desire - Action and Creation - Provision - Speech. (They) i.e. His eternal attributes. (Knowledge) is an eternal attribute by which known things are disclosed when it relates to them. (Power) is an eternal attribute that affects the objects of power when it relates to them. Commentary
This passage first lists the eternal attributes of Allah: knowledge, power, life, strength, hearing, sight, will, desire, action, creation, provision, and speech. Then it begins defining them. The definition of knowledge (العلم) is that it is an eternal attribute that causes known things to become disclosed when it relates to them. Power (القدرة) is an eternal attribute that affects the objects of power when it relates to them. Life (الحياة) is an eternal attribute that makes knowledge correct. Strength (القوة) is said to be the same as power, but the text includes an unclear phrase 'from other than Sari'. These definitions emphasize that the attributes are eternal in themselves and their effects occur upon relation to their objects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Allah's attributes are mere names without real meaning or that they are temporal.
Correction: Taftazani defines them as real eternal attributes that have specific effects, showing they are not mere names.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of knowledge (العلم) as an attribute of Allah?
A) An attribute by which known things are created.
B) An eternal attribute by which known things are disclosed when it relates to them.
C) An attribute that necessitates power.
D) An attribute that exists only temporally.

Key Takeaway
Allah's eternal attributes are real; knowledge discloses, power affects, life enables, and strength is like power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's knowledge discloses everything you do, how would it change your actions today? What would you stop doing? What would you start? Commit to one change.
?
Allah's power affects all objects; reflect on a situation where you felt powerless. How does knowing that Allah's power is eternal and affects all things change your perspective? Will you rely on Him differently?
?
The attribute of life necessitates soundness of knowledge; if your own life is sustained by Him, how does that impact your pursuit of knowledge? Are you seeking beneficial knowledge that brings you closer to Him? Make a promise to Allah about your study.

Eternal Attributes: Hearing and Sight
Taftazani defines hearing and sight and refutes the entailment objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how divine hearing and sight are defined as eternal attributes that relate to temporal objects without requiring the pre-eternity of those objects.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes relate to temporal things without being temporal themselves.

In this passage, Taftazani defines the divine attributes of hearing and sight, emphasizing that they are perfect perceptions not dependent on physical organs. He then addresses a potential confusion: if these attributes are eternal, wouldn't their objects also be eternal? His response clarifies an important principle about eternal attributes and their relations to temporal things.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions
Carefully read Taftazani's definitions of hearing and sight. Notice that he specifies these are perfect perceptions, not based on imagination, sense organs, or physical medium like air.
The definition of sight explicitly negates any physical process.
2
Understand the objection
Identify the potential objection: if hearing and sight are eternal, then their objects (sounds and visible things) would also have to be eternal. Why might someone think that?
This objection arises from a misunderstanding of how attributes relate to their objects.
3
Grasp the refutation
Study Taftazani's response: the eternity of the attribute does not necessitate the eternity of its objects. He uses the analogy of knowledge and power. The key is that attributes are eternal but acquire relations (tacalluq) to temporal objects when those objects exist.
This principle safeguards divine transcendence while affirming real attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( والسمع ) وهي صفة تتعلق بالمسموعات .
(والبصر) وهى صفة تتعلق بالمبصرات فتدرك إدراكا تاما لا على سبيل التخيل أو التوهم ولا على طريق تأثير حاسة ووصول هواء.
ولا يلزم من قدمهما قدم المسموعات والمبصرات، كما لا يلزم من قدم العلم والقدرة قدم المعلومات والمقدورات، لأنها صفات قديمة تحدث لها تعلقات بالحوادث.
(Hearing) is an attribute that relates to heard things. (Sight) is an attribute that relates to seen things, and it perceives them completely, not by way of imagination or illusion, nor by the effect of a sense organ or the arrival of air. And their pre-eternity does not necessitate the pre-eternity of heard and seen things, just as the pre-eternity of knowledge and power does not necessitate the pre-eternity of known things and objects of power, because they are eternal attributes that acquire relations to temporal things when those relations occur.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage defines the attributes of hearing (السمع) and sight (البصر). Hearing relates to sounds, and sight relates to visible things, perceiving them fully, not through imagination, not through an organ or physical medium like air. Then it addresses a potential objection: if these attributes are eternal, would not their objects (sounds and visible things) also have to be eternal? The author replies that this does not follow, just as the eternity of knowledge and power does not require that known things and objects of power be eternal. The reason is that these are eternal attributes that, despite being eternal, acquire relations (تعلقات) to temporal objects when those objects come into existence. So the attribute remains eternal, but its relation to a particular object occurs in time.

Key Terms
السمع
البصر
قدم الصفات
التعلقات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If hearing is eternal, then everything heard must also be eternal.
Correction: Hearing is an eternal attribute, but its relation to particular sounds occurs only when those sounds exist. The attribute is eternal in itself, but its taʿalluq (relation) is temporal.

Checkpoint
Why does the eternity of hearing and sight not require the eternity of heard and seen things?
A) Because hearing and sight are not real attributes.
B) Because these attributes are eternal but acquire relations to temporal things.
C) Because heard and seen things are also eternal.
D) Because the attributes are temporal.

Key Takeaway
Divine hearing and sight are eternal, perfect perceptions; their relations to temporal objects do not make the objects eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that God hears your whispered excuse and sees your hidden action right now, not as a distant record but as a present, perfect perception? How would your next hour change if you lived in that awareness?
?

If that is real, why do you still live as though your private thoughts and secret deeds are hidden from Him? What would it cost you to confess that you know He sees and still choose to turn away?
?
The passage frees God's attributes from the limits of created perception. If God does not hear or see as creatures do, then your relationship with Him cannot be built on mere ritual or imagination. Are you willing to seek a direct, unmediated intimacy with the One whose perception is absolute? What needs to change in your daily life for that to begin?

The Divine Attribute of Will and Desire
Taftazani defines will/desire and refutes two false interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's will is a distinct eternal attribute that specifies what occurs, and why it is not merely command or a temporal accident.

Core Idea
Allah's will is the attribute that makes one possibility happen, not just a command.

This passage from Taftazani defines the attribute of will (iradah) and desire (mashiyyah) as one and the same eternal attribute in Allah. He then refutes two incorrect views that either split will into eternal and temporal or reduce it to mere command. Understanding this attribute is crucial for a correct theology of divine action and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the definition of will/desire as an attribute that specifies one of two possible things to occur at a particular time despite equal relation of power.
Notice that knowledge follows occurrence, not the other way around.
2
Analyze the first refutation
Identify the claim that mashiyyah is eternal and iradah is temporal. Understand why this is false based on the passage's hint that both are expressions of the same attribute.
3
Analyze the second refutation
Identify the claim that will for Allah's own act is merely negative (not coerced, etc.) and for another's act is just command. See how the passage refutes this by noting that Allah commands all to believe but not all believe.
The example of commanding belief shows will is not identical to command.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how the correct understanding of Allah's will impacts our view of divine decree (qadar) and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والإرادة والمشيئة) وهما عبارتان عن صفة في الحي، توجب تخصيص أحد المقدورين فى أحد الأوقات بالوقوع مع استواء نسبة القدرة إلى الكل. وكون تعلق العلم تابعا للوقوع .
وفيما ذكر تنبيه على الرد على من زعم أن المشيئة قديمة والإرادة حادثة قائمة بذات الله تعالى .
وعلى من زعم أن معنى إرادة الله تعالى فعله : أنه ليس بمكره ولا ساه ولا مغلوب .
ومعنى إرادته فعل غيره أنه أمر به. كيف ؟ وقد أمر كل مكلف بالإيمان وسائر الواجبات. ولو شاء لوقع.
(Will and Desire) are both expressions for an attribute in the Living (Allah) that necessitates the specification of one of two possible things to occur at a particular time, despite the equal relation of power to all. And that the relation of knowledge is subsequent to occurrence. In what has been mentioned is a hint at refuting those who claim that desire (mashiyyah) is eternal and will (iradah) is temporal and subsisting in Allah's essence. And also those who claim that the meaning of Allah's will regarding His own act is that He is not coerced, nor heedless, nor overcome. And the meaning of His will regarding the act of another is that He commands it. How? He has commanded every morally responsible person to believe and all obligatory acts. And if He willed, it would occur.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage defines will and desire as one attribute that specifies the occurrence of one of two equally possible things at a specific time, despite power being equally related to both. Knowledge then follows the occurrence. Then it refutes two wrong views: (1) Those who claim that مشيئة (mashiyyah) is eternal while إرادة (iradah) is created and subsists in Allah's essence. (2) Those who claim that when Allah's will applies to His own act, it only means He is not coerced, careless, or defeated. The correct view is that His will for another's act means He commands that act. But if that were simply the command, then everyone would obey? The text says He commanded every accountable person to believe and do obligations, but if He had willed (absolute will) they would have occurred. This shows that will is not merely command; it is a distinct attribute that determines occurrence.

Key Terms
الإرادة
المشيئة
تخصيص المقدور
الأمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah's will (iradah) is merely a command (amr) or a negative attribute (e.g., not coerced).
Correction: The text shows that Allah commands all to believe, but He does not will that every person actually believes; otherwise they would. So will is a distinct determining attribute, not reducible to command or negation.

Checkpoint
What does the attribute of will (الإرادة) do according to this passage?
A) It creates all things directly.
B) It specifies one of two equal possibilities to occur at a particular time.
C) It merely indicates command.
D) It is the same as knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Allah's will is a real eternal attribute that determines the occurrence of events, distinct from both power and command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that everything that happens, including your own sins, occurs by Allah's will? How does this reality affect your repentance and hope in His mercy?
?
If Allah commands you to do something but you fail, do you attribute your failure to your own weakness or realize that ultimately His will overrides? How should that shape your humility before Him?
?
The passage refutes those who treat Allah's will as a mere absence of coercion. Are there areas in your life where you treat Allah's will as passive or indifferent rather than active and decisive? What needs to change in your view of His sovereignty?

Eternal Attribute of Action: Takwin
Taftazani defines action and creation (takwin) and provision, refuting the Ash'ari view of them as relational.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine action attributes like creation and provision are not separate but expressions of a single eternal attribute called takwin, contrary to the Ash'ari view.

Core Idea
All divine actions reduce to one eternal attribute: takwin.

Taftazani clarifies that when we speak of Allah's actions—creating, providing, giving life, causing death—these are not multiple distinct attributes. Rather, they all refer to a single eternal attribute subsisting in Allah's essence, called takwin. This lesson examines the definition and the refutation of the Ash'ari position that these are mere relations or attributes of actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Note the key terms: التكوين, التخليق, الترزيق, and the reference to الأشعرى.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the two competing views
The passage presents two views: (1) the correct view that all action attributes reduce to one eternal attribute (takwin), and (2) the Ash'ari view that they are relations and attributes of actions. Identify the wording for each.
3
Understand the reduction
Notice that the author lists several action attributes (creation, provision, forming, etc.) and says each is a specific takwin. Grasp how this unifies the attributes under one eternal attribute.
This is a core Maturidi doctrine distinguishing them from Ash'aris.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والفعل والتخليق) عبارة عن صفة أزلية تسمى التكوين. وسيجي تحقيقه.
وعدل عن لفظ الخلق لشيوع استعماله في المخلوق .
(والترزيق هو تكوين مخصوص، صرح به إشارة إلى أن مثل التخليق والترزيق والتصوير والإحياء والإماتة . وغير ذلك . مما أسند إلى الله تعالى : كل منها راجع إلى صفة حقيقية أزلية قائمة بالذات هي التكوين لا كما زعم الأشعرى ) من أنها إضافات وصفات للأفعال .
(Action and Creation) are expressions for an eternal attribute called takwin (bringing into existence). Its verification will come later. And the term creation (khalq) was avoided due to its common usage for the created thing. (Provision) is a specific takwin, mentioned explicitly to indicate that such things as creation, provision, forming, giving life, causing death, and others that are attributed to Allah — each refers to a real eternal attribute subsisting in the essence, which is takwin, not as the Ash'ari claimed, that they are relations and attributes of actions.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage discusses the attributes of action (فعل) and creation (تخليق). These are expressions for a single eternal attribute called التكوين (bringing into existence). The author notes that the word 'خلق' is avoided here because it is commonly used for the created thing itself. Then provision (ترزيق) is described as a specific kind of takwin. The point is that all such action-related attributes (creation, provision, forming, giving life, causing death, etc.) are actually one real eternal attribute subsisting in Allah's essence, namely takwin. This refutes the Ash'ari position that these are mere relations (إضافات) or attributes of actions (صفات للأفعال). Instead, they are rooted in a single attribute of the essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Each divine action (creating, providing, etc.) is a separate eternal attribute.
Correction: All action attributes are expressions of one eternal attribute: takwin.

Checkpoint
What is the Ash'ari view on action attributes like creation and provision?
A) They are one attribute called takwin.
B) They are relations (idafat) and attributes of actions.
C) They are temporal and not eternal.
D) They are identical to knowledge.

Key Takeaway
All divine action attributes reduce to one eternal attribute, takwin, not to mere relations as Ash'aris claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Allah brings forth the living from the dead,' do you pause to realize that this act is not a separate event but flows from an eternal attribute that never changes? How would your awe of Him deepen if you remembered that the same attribute that creates is also the one that provides and gives life?
?
The Ash'aris saw Allah's actions as mere relations to created things. Have you ever treated your relationship with Allah as only a series of events, forgetting that beneath every act is an unchanging essence? What would it mean for your trust in Him to know that His giving and taking are not passing moods but expressions of an eternal attribute?
?
You affirm this truth in your creed, but does your heart feel the weight that every provision, every breath, every moment of life is a direct expression of the same eternal attribute of takwin? If you truly believed this, how would it change your gratitude, your patience, and your reliance on Allah?

Allah's Speech as an Eternal Internal Attribute
Taftazani defines speech as eternal attribute and distinguishes from knowledge and will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attribute of speech (kalam) is an eternal internal meaning distinct from knowledge and will, and that the Quran is its expression.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is an eternal internal meaning, not the same as the Quranic text.

Taftazani begins by defining Allah's speech as an eternal attribute that is expressed through the Quran. He then argues that this speech is distinct from both knowledge and will, using logical reasoning and a poetic reference. This passage lays the foundation for understanding the nature of the Quran as the created expression of an uncreated attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the definition of speech as an eternal attribute.
Notice that Taftazani immediately links it to the Quran as its expression.
2
Identify the distinctions
Find where Taftazani distinguishes speech from knowledge and from will. He gives examples for each.
The distinction from will is illustrated with a command that is not willed.
3
Consider the evidence
Reflect on the example of commanding a servant to show disobedience, and the verse from al-Akhtal. How do these support the distinction?
4
Connect to doctrine
Understand that this teaching establishes the Quran as the expression of an eternal attribute, guarding against the view that the Quran itself is eternal or that Allah's speech is temporal.
This is a key point in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والكلام) هو صفة أزلية عبر عنها بالنظم المسمى بالقرآن المركب من الحروف. وذلك لأن كل من يأمر وينهي ويخبر يجد في نفسه معنى. ثم يدل عليه بالعبارة أو الكتابة أو الإشارة وهو غير .العلم. إذ قد يخبر الإنسان عما لا يعلمه، بل يعلم خلافه. وغير الإرادة لأنه قد يأمر بما لا يريده .(۱) . كمن أمر عبده قصدا لإظهار عصيانه وعدم امتثاله لأوامره ويسمى هذا كلاما نفسيا على ما أشار إليه الأخطل بقوله : (۱) كما يأمر الكفرة بالإيمان مثلا وهو لا يريد منهم الإيمان فلا يقع.
(Speech) is an eternal attribute expressed by the composition called the Quran composed of letters. This is because everyone who commands, forbids, or informs finds in himself a meaning. Then he indicates it by expression, writing, or gesture. And it is not knowledge. For a person may inform about something he does not know, but rather knows the opposite. And it is not will, because he may command what he does not will. Like one who commands his servant deliberately to show his disobedience and non-compliance with his orders. This is called internal speech (kalam nafsi), as indicated by al-Akhtal in his verse. (1) As when He commands the disbelievers to believe, for example, while He does not will faith from them, so it does not occur.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage defines speech (الكلام) as an eternal attribute of Allah, which is expressed through the composition of the Quran made of letters. The argument is that anyone who commands, forbids, or informs finds an internal meaning in himself, and then expresses it through words, writing, or signs. This internal meaning is what is called speech, and it is distinct from knowledge because a person can inform about something he does not know or knows the opposite. It is also distinct from will because a person can command what he does not will, like a master commanding his servant intentionally to show the servant's disobedience. This is called internal speech (كلام نفسي). The author cites the poet al-Akhtal to support this concept. A footnote clarifies that Allah commands the disbelievers to believe while not willing faith from them (since He knows they will not believe), so the command is issued but the act does not occur, proving that speech is not the same as will.

Key Terms
الكلام
الكلام النفسي
القرآن
الأخطل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some equate Allah's speech with the Quranic text itself, thinking the Quran is uncreated in its letters and sounds.
Correction: This passage teaches that the eternal attribute is the internal meaning (kalam nafsi), while the Arabic Quran is its expression. The Quran is created as a composition of letters, but the attribute of speech is uncreated.

Checkpoint
What evidence does the passage give to show that speech is not the same as will?
A) Speech is composed of letters while will is not.
B) A person may command what he does not will.
C) Speech is eternal while will is temporal.
D) The Quran is created.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is an eternal internal attribute, expressed by the Quran, and distinct from knowledge and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What is one area in your life where you have been striving as if your command or desire automatically brings about change, instead of relying on Allah's will to make it happen? Write down a specific change you will make to align your efforts with true tawakkul.
?
The passage teaches that speech (the internal meaning) is distinct from its outward expression. When you recite the Quran or make du'a, do you tend to focus more on the words or on the inward reality they express? What is one concrete step you can take in your next prayer or recitation to truly connect your heart's meaning with your tongue's utterance?
?
If Allah's speech is eternal and not dependent on creation, how should this elevate the reverence you feel when you hear or recite the Quran? Are you treating the Quran merely as a book or as a connection to the eternal attribute of your Lord? What is one change in your daily interaction with the Quran that will reflect this higher station?

Divine Attributes

Refutation of Claims about Divine Will
Refutes two erroneous views on divine will and intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between will (mashi'a) and intention (irada) in Allah, and the refutation of claims that they differ in eternity or that intention is merely command.

Core Idea
Allah's will and intention are co-eternal, and His command is distinct from His intention.

This passage from the Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah addresses two common misconceptions about divine will. The first separates eternal will from created intention, while the second conflates intention with command. Understanding these distinctions is essential for preserving the transcendence of Allah's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation to get the overall flow of the argument. Notice that the author refutes two distinct claims.
The passage begins with 'وفيما ذكر تنبيه على الرد...'
2
Identify the two refuted views
Pinpoint the two erroneous positions: (1) that al-mashi'a is eternal but al-irada is created, and (2) that Allah's intention for His own act means He is not coerced, while for another's act it means He commands it.
These views are presented concisely; distinguish them clearly.
3
Analyze the evidence provided
Notice how the author uses the example of commanding faith and obligations: Allah commands all individuals to believe, yet He does not will that all believe, which shows command is not identical to intention.
The phrase 'ولو شاء لوقع' emphasizes that if Allah willed it, it would occur, but He does not will it for all.
4
Reflect on the theological implications
Consider why these distinctions matter: they protect Allah's attributes from limitations and affirm that His will and intention are eternal and perfect, while His commands serve a different purpose.
This reinforces the principle that nothing in Allah's attributes is created or subject to change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيما ذكر تنبيه على الرد على من زعم أن المشيئة قديمة والإرادة حادثة قائمة بذات الله تعالى . وعلى من زعم أن معنى إرادة الله تعالى فعله : أنه ليس بمكره ولا ساه ولا مغلوب . ومعنى إرادته فعل غيره أنه أمر به. كيف ؟ وقد أمر كل مكلف بالإيمان وسائر الواجبات. ولو شاء لوقع.
And in what was mentioned is a reminder of the refutation of those who claim that the will (al-mashi'a) is eternal and the intention (al-irada) is created, subsisting in the essence of Allah most high. And of those who claim that the meaning of Allah's intention for His own act is that He is not coerced, nor heedless, nor overcome. And the meaning of His intention for the act of another is that He commanded it. How? And indeed He commanded every responsible person to faith and all obligations. And if He willed, it would occur.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two erroneous views concerning God's will and intention. First, it refutes those who assert that the will (mashi'a) is eternal but intention (irada) is a created attribute subsisting in God's essence. Second, it refutes those who claim that God's intention for His own act means He is not coerced, heedless, or overcome—that is, it is an attribute of perfection. The passage then explains the meaning of God's intention for another's act: it is simply His command. This is demonstrated by the fact that God commands every responsible person to believe and perform obligations, yet if He willed that they disobey, that would also occur, showing that command is distinct from intention.

Key Terms
المشيئة
الإرادة
المكره

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's intention for another's act is identical to His command, meaning that if God commands something, He must will it to happen.
Correction: This passage shows that command is distinct from intention; God can command something without willing it to occur, as seen when He commands faith but some do not believe.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the meaning of God's intention (irada) for the act of another?
A) It means He wills that act to occur
B) It means He commands that act
C) It means He approves of that act
D) It means He is not coerced

Key Takeaway
The intention and will of Allah are co-eternal and distinct from His command; command does not imply occurrence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that Allah commands you to pray, but you sometimes miss it. Does your missing prove that Allah did not will you to pray? How does this lesson change your understanding of the relationship between God's command and His will? What will you do today to align your will with His command?
?
Do you ever excuse your sin by saying 'It was Allah's will'? This lesson says Allah's command is distinct from His will. How does that affect your responsibility for your choices? Are you ready to stop blaming God and start obeying?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's intention for your actions is broader than His commands, would you take your obedience more seriously? What specific step will you take this week to obey a command you have been neglecting?

4 min
Takwin: The Single Eternal Attribute Behind All Divine Acts
Defines takwin as an eternal attribute and refutes Ash'ari view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all divine creative acts (creating, providing, forming, giving life, etc.) are manifestations of one eternal attribute called takwin, refuting the Ash'ari view that they are mere relations.

Core Idea
All divine acts flow from one eternal attribute: takwīn.

This lesson examines the Maturidi definition of takwin (creative power) as an eternal attribute of Allah. The author clarifies that terms like 'creating' and 'providing' refer not to multiple attributes but to specific instances of this single attribute. This directly opposes the Ash'ari position that such acts are merely relational.

Guided Path
1
Meet the key term: takwīn
Read the first line where takwīn is introduced as an eternal attribute. Note that 'action' and 'creating' (al-takhlīq) are expressions for it.
2
Distinguish khalq from takwīn
The author deliberately avoids the term 'khalq' because it is commonly used for the created thing, not the creative power. Understand this subtle shift in vocabulary.
3
See takwīn in specific acts
The passage states that 'providing' (al-tarzīq) is a specific takwīn. Then it lists other acts (forming, giving life, etc.) and declares each refers back to the same eternal attribute.
This shows the unity of God's creative power.
4
Contrast with the Ash'arī view
The passage explicitly refutes al-Ash'ari's claim that these are mere relations or attributes of acts. Understand why the Maturidi position insists on a real, eternal attribute.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider why it matters that all creative acts stem from one attribute: it preserves God's simplicity and eternal power, avoiding multiplicity in the divine essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفعل والتخليق) عبارة عن صفة أزلية تسمى التكوين. وسيجي تحقيقه. وعدل عن لفظ الخلق لشيوع استعماله في المخلوق . (والترزيق هو تكوين مخصوص، صرح به إشارة إلى أن مثل التخليق والترزيق والتصوير والإحياء والإماتة . وغير ذلك . مما أسند إلى الله تعالى : كل منها راجع إلى صفة حقيقية أزلية قائمة بالذات هي التكوين لا كما زعم الأشعرى ) من أنها إضافات وصفات للأفعال .
And 'action' and 'creating' (al-takhlīq) are expressions for an eternal attribute called takwīn (creative power). And its verification will come. And he turned away from the term al-khalq because of its common usage for the created thing. And 'providing' (al-tarzīq) is a specific takwīn. He stated this explicitly as an indication that such as creating, providing, forming, giving life, and causing death, and other things attributed to Allah most high, each of them refers back to a real eternal attribute subsisting in the essence, which is takwīn, not as al-Ash'ari claimed, that they are relations and attributes of acts.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage provides the definition of takwīn (creative power) as an eternal attribute of God distinct from the created things themselves. The author explains that terms like 'creating' (takhlīq) and 'action' (fi'l) refer to this attribute. He deliberately avoids the term 'khalq' because it is commonly used for the created entity. Similarly, 'providing' (tarzīq) is a specific instance of takwīn. The point is that all divine acts such as creating, providing, forming, giving life, and causing death are not multiple attributes but manifestations of one single eternal attribute: takwīn. This refutes the Ash'ari position that these are merely relational attributes or attributes of acts.

التخليق
الترزيق

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Each divine act (creating, providing, etc.) is a separate, independent attribute of God.
Correction: The passage teaches that all such acts are specific instances of one eternal attribute: takwīn.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how are acts like creating, providing, and giving life related to the attribute of takwīn?
A) They are different attributes
B) They are relations, not real attributes
C) They are specific instances of takwīn
D) They are created temporal acts

Key Takeaway
Takwin is the single eternal attribute of creative power, from which all specific divine acts emanate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness an act of providing or creating in your life, do you instinctively attribute it to a single, eternal power of Allah, or do you see it as a disconnected event? How can you train your heart to see all divine acts as flowing from the same eternal attribute takwīn, and what would change in your gratitude and reliance on Him?
?
The Ash'ari view reduces divine acts to mere relations. In your daily gratitude, do you treat Allah's provisions and creations as real, direct acts of His power, or are you prone to abstract them? What concrete step can you take today to affirm the reality of His attribute takwīn in your supplications and reflections?

Divine Speech as an Eternal Attribute
Defines divine speech and introduces inner meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine speech is an eternal attribute expressed through the Quran, and that every command, prohibition, or information originates from an inner meaning.

Core Idea
Divine speech is an eternal attribute, not a created sequence of sounds.

The author begins by defining divine speech (al-kalām) as an eternal attribute of Allah, expressed through the Quran. He grounds this definition in a universal human experience: everyone who commands, forbids, or informs finds an inner meaning before expressing it. This lesson establishes the fundamental nature of God's speech as uncreated and subsisting in His essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice that divine speech is described as an eternal attribute, not a created entity. The Quran is the expression of this attribute.
2
Understand the experiential argument
The author argues that every person who commands, forbids, or informs first finds an inner meaning. This shows that speech is not merely outward expression but has an inner reality.
3
Reflect on the implication
If human speech has an inner dimension, then divine speech, which is eternal, must also have an inner reality beyond the letters and sounds of the Quran.
This prepares for the distinction from knowledge and will in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكلام) هو صفة أزلية عبر عنها بالنظم المسمى بالقرآن المركب من الحروف. وذلك لأن كل من يأمر وينهي ويخبر يجد في نفسه معنى. ثم يدل عليه بالعبارة أو الكتابة أو الإشارة وهو غير العلم. إذ قد يخبر الإنسان عما لا يعلمه، بل يعلم خلافه. وغير الإرادة لأنه قد يأمر بما لا يريده . كمن أمر عبده قصدا لإظهار عصيانه وعدم امتثاله لأوامره ويسمى هذا كلاما نفسيا على ما أشار إليه الأخطل بقوله : إن الكلام لفى الفؤاد وإنما جعل اللسان على الفؤاد دليلا وقال عمر رضى الله عنه : إنى زورت في نفسي مقالة . وكثيرا ما تقول لصاحبك : إن فى نفسى كلاما أريد أن أذكره لك . والدليل على ثبوت صفة الكلام : إجماع الأمة وتواتر النقل عن الانبياء - عليهم السلام - أنه تعالى متكلم، مع القطع باستحالة التكلم من غير ثبوت صفة الكلام .
And 'speech' (al-kalām) is an eternal attribute expressed by the composition called al-Qur'an, composed of letters. This is because everyone who commands, forbids, and informs finds within himself a meaning. Then he indicates it by expression, writing, or gesture. And it is different from knowledge, for a person may inform about something he does not know, but rather knows its opposite. And it is different from will, for he may command what he does not will, like one who commands his slave deliberately to show his disobedience and failure to comply with his orders. And this is called internal speech (kalām nafsī), as al-Akhtal pointed out in his verse: 'Indeed speech is in the heart / And the tongue is only made a guide to the heart.' And 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'I prepared in myself a statement.' And often you say to your companion: 'I have some speech in myself that I want to mention to you.' And the proof for the establishment of the attribute of speech is the consensus of the community and the frequent transmission from the prophets (peace be upon them) that He, exalted, is speaking, along with the certainty of the impossibility of speaking without the establishment of the attribute of speech.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage defines divine speech (kalām) as an eternal attribute of God, expressed through the sequential composition of letters that we call the Quran. The author gives an experiential argument: every person who commands, forbids, or informs has an inner meaning (ma'nā) which he then expresses through words, writing, or gesture. This inner meaning is distinct from knowledge, because one can speak about something one does not know or even knows to be false. It is also distinct from will, because one can command something one does not will, as when a master commands his slave to test his obedience. This inner speech is called 'kalām nafsī', supported by al-Akhtal's poetry and the statement of Umar. The formal proof for the attribute of divine speech is the consensus of the Muslim community and the widespread transmission from the prophets that God is 'speaking' (mutakallim), combined with the necessary impossibility of ascribing speech to God without a real attribute of speech subsisting in His essence.

Key Terms
الكلام
المعنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the Quran in relation to divine speech?
A) It is the eternal attribute itself.
B) It is the created expression of the eternal attribute.
C) It is a metaphor for God's knowledge.
D) It is the same as the inner meaning.

Key Takeaway
Divine speech is an eternal attribute of Allah, and the Quran is its created expression in letters and sounds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you experience it as merely a sequence of letters or do you sense the eternal speech of Allah? How would your recitation change if you fully internalized that each verse is an expression of an uncreated attribute?
?
The passage shows that every command, prohibition, or piece of information originates from an inner meaning before being uttered. How aware are you of the intentions behind your own words? Do your words accurately reflect your inner meanings, or is there disconnect?
?
If divine speech is eternal and the Quran is its temporal expression, then every time you read the Quran you are encountering an eternal reality in time. Does this understanding deepen your reverence for the Quran? What practical steps can you take today to treat the Quran with the awe it deserves as the expression of Allah’s eternal attribute?

How Divine Speech Differs from Knowledge and Will
Distinguishes divine speech from knowledge and will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine speech is distinct from both knowledge and will, and you will grasp the rational basis for these distinctions.

Core Idea
Speech is not knowledge or will—one can inform of falsehoods and command what one does not will.

Having defined divine speech as an eternal attribute, the author now distinguishes it from two other divine attributes: knowledge and will. He gives concrete examples: a person can inform about something he does not know, and a master may command his slave to test his obedience without actually willing that action. These distinctions clarify that speech is a unique attribute subsisting in God's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the distinction from knowledge
Read the Arabic for the distinction from knowledge. Note the example: a person may inform about something he does not know, even knows to be false.
2
Read the distinction from will
Read the Arabic for the distinction from will. The example is a master commanding a slave to show disobedience, not actually willing the command to be obeyed.
3
Understand the implications for divine speech
If human speech can be independent of knowledge and will, then divine speech is also distinct from these attributes. This preserves the uniqueness of each divine attribute.

Internal Speech (Kalām Nafsī) and Its Proof
Introduces internal speech and provides proof for attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of internal speech (kalām nafsī) as the inner meaning, and you will learn the main evidence for the attribute of speech in God.

Core Idea
True speech is in the heart; the tongue is its guide.

After distinguishing speech from knowledge and will, the author introduces the term 'internal speech' (kalām nafsī), which is the inner meaning that exists in the soul. He supports this with poetry, a statement of Umar, and common experience. Finally, he presents the theological proof for the attribute of speech: the consensus of the Muslim community and the frequent reports from prophets that God speaks, combined with the logical impossibility of speaking without an attribute of speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the concept of internal speech
Read the Arabic introducing 'kalām nafsī' and the supporting examples: al-Akhtal's verse, Umar's statement, and everyday language.
2
Analyze the proof
Read the proof section. It relies on consensus (ijma) and transmitted reports (tawatur) that God is 'speaking', plus the rational principle that speaking requires an attribute.
3
Reflect on the significance
Internal speech shows that divine speech is not merely outward expression but an eternal meaning subsisting in God's essence. The proof establishes that this attribute is real.

Source Text

The Eight Essential Attributes of Allah
Enumerates the eight essential attributes of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to name the eight essential attributes of Allah as enumerated by Imam al-Nasafi and understand their foundational role in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Allah's eight attributes are the building blocks of all theological discourse.

This passage marks a pivotal moment in the study of divine attributes. After earlier arguments, Imam al-Nasafi concludes that Allah possesses eight essential attributes. Memorizing this list is not just a memory exercise—it is the foundation for understanding how Muslim theologians have discussed God's nature. As you read, pay close attention to the order and the Arabic terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage aloud
Read the Arabic sentence and its English translation. Note the rhythm and the terms used.
2
Identify each attribute
Write down all eight attributes in Arabic and English. Compare with the key terms provided.
These are all eternal essential attributes.
3
Understand the significance
Ask yourself: Why are these eight considered essential? What distinguishes them from other attributes mentioned elsewhere?
The commentary hints that three are more controversial.
4
Reflect on the controversy
Notice that 'irada', 'takwin', and 'kalam' are highlighted as potentially obscure. Research or discuss why these might be debated.
This connects to later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فثبت : ان الله تعالى صفات ثمانية : هى : العلم والقدرة، والحياة ،والسمع والبصر، والإرادة والتكوين والكلام
So it is established that Allah most high has eight attributes: knowledge, power, life, hearing, sight, will, creative power (takwīn), and speech (kalām).
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion that lists the eight essential attributes of Allah as established in earlier discussions. The attributes are: knowledge ('ilm), power (qudra), life (hayāh), hearing (sam'), sight (baṣar), will (irāda), creative power (takwīn), and speech (kalām). The author implicitly notes that three of these—irada, takwin, and kalam—have generated more controversy and obscurity, as the subsequent passage elaborates.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Allah has only seven essential attributes, or that some attributes are not distinct from others.
Correction: This passage explicitly states eight attributes. In Maturidi theology, each is a distinct eternal attribute of the essence, not reducible to others.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Allah possesses eight essential, eternal attributes: knowledge, power, life, hearing, sight, will, creative power, and speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Divine Speech: Eternal Attribute, Not Letters
Detailed proof that divine speech is eternal and non-composite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine speech is an eternal attribute of Allah, distinct from created letters and sounds.

Core Idea
Divine speech is eternal, not a sequence of temporal sounds.

This lesson unpacks the detailed proof for the attribute of speech. The author presents three essential claims: that speech is a necessary attribute of God, that it is eternal, and that it is not composed of letters and sounds. Each claim is supported by a rational necessity, culminating in a clear refutation of the Mu'tazilite position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Get a feel for the concise, logical style of the author.
Notice that the passage opens by explaining why the author elaborates on the last three attributes.
2
Understand the first proof: Speech as attribute
Focus on why a derived term like 'speaking' requires that the source of derivation (speech) subsist in the one described. This refutes the Mu'tazila who place speech in a substrate other than God.
The principle is: you cannot call someone 'speaking' unless speech truly belongs to them.
3
Grasp the second proof: Eternity of speech
Read the claim that speech is eternal because temporal accidents cannot subsist in Allah's essence. This is a direct application of the principle that God's essence cannot be a locus for originated things.
4
Analyze the third proof: Not letters/sounds
Understand the argument that letters and sounds are temporal, each requiring the prior one to cease. Since divine speech is eternal, it cannot be of this nature.
The impossibility of uttering the second letter without the first ending is said to be self-evident.
5
Connect to the common misunderstanding
Reflect on the common misconception that the Quran's composed nature implies God's speech is composed. The lesson shows that the attribute itself is simple and eternal; the Quran is the expression of that attribute in created form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما كان في الثلاثة الأخيرة زيادة نزاع وخفاء، كرر الإشارة إلى إثباتها وقدمها . وفصل الكلام بعض التفصيل فقال : (وهو) أى الله تعالى متكلم بكلام ، هو صفة له ضرورة : امتناع إثبات المشتق للشيء من غير قيام ماخذ الاشتقاق به. وفى هذا رد على المعتزلة، حيث ذهبوا إلى أنه متكلم بكلام هو قائم بغيره، ليس صفة له . (أزلية) ضرورة امتناع قيام الحوادث بذاته . ليس من جنس الحروف والأصوات ضرورة أنها أعراض حادثة مشروط حدوث بعضها بانقضاء البعض، لأن امتناع التكلم بالحرف الثاني بدون انقضاء الحرف الأول بديهى.
And since in the last three there is increased controversy and obscurity, he repeated the indication of their establishment and gave them precedence. And he detailed speech with some elaboration and said: 'And He' i.e. Allah most high is speaking with speech, which is an attribute for Him necessarily: because of the impossibility of establishing a derived term for something without the source of derivation subsisting in it. And in this is a refutation of the Mu'tazila, as they held that He is speaking with speech subsisting in another, not an attribute for Him. 'Eternal' necessarily because of the impossibility of temporal things subsisting in His essence. 'Not of the genus of letters and sounds' necessarily because they are temporal accidents whose occurrence is conditional upon the passing away of some for others, for the impossibility of speaking the second letter without the passing of the first is self-evident.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed proof for the speech attribute, specifically addressing the last three attributes (irada, takwin, kalam) that are more controversial. The author repeats the proof for these three and elaborates on speech. He asserts that God is 'speaking' (mutakallim) with speech that is His attribute. The logical basis is that a derived term like 'speaking' cannot be applied to something unless the source of derivation (speech) subsists in it. This refutes the Mu'tazila who claim that God's speech is a created entity subsisting in something other than God (e.g., the Quran as a created accident in a substrate). Next, he affirms that this speech is eternal, because temporal accidents cannot subsist in God's essence. Finally, he clarifies that this speech is not composed of letters and sounds, because letters and sounds are temporal accidents that are contingent on the passing of previous ones—the impossibility of speaking the second letter before the first ends is self-evident. Thus, divine speech is a single eternal attribute, not a sequence.

Key Terms
المشتق
مأخذ الاشتقاق
الحروف والأصوات

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's letters and sounds are part of God's eternal speech itself.
Correction: Divine speech is an eternal attribute, not composed of letters and sounds which are temporal accidents. The Quran's letters and sounds are created expressions of that attribute.

Checkpoint

C) Because God does not speak in Arabic

What needs to change today so that you hear each ayah as addressed to you by the Eternal Speaker?

Proof of the Divine Attribute of Speech
The author provides evidence for the attribute of speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author proves that speech is a real attribute of Allah using consensus and uninterrupted transmission from the prophets.

Core Idea
God's speech is proven by flawless consensus, not mere metaphor.

This lesson examines the evidence for the attribute of speech. The author begins by establishing that speech is an internal reality, quoting a poetic line and a statement from Umar. He then presents the logical proof based on community consensus and prophetic transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about speech in the heart
Read the first part of the Arabic passage: the poetic verse and Umar's saying. Notice that speech is described as something internal to the person, with the tongue serving as an external proof.
This sets the stage for the attribute being real.
2
Identify the formal proof
Locate the sentence that begins with 'الدليل على ثبوت صفة الكلام'. Understand that the proof consists of two elements: consensus of the community (ijma') and continuous transmission (tawatur) from the prophets that God is speaking.
This is a standard kalam argument: if God is described as speaking, and speech is an attribute, then the attribute must exist.
3
Understand the logical necessity
Reflect on the final phrase: 'مع القطع باستحالة التكلم من غير ثبوت صفة الكلام'. It is impossible for God to be described as speaking without the attribute of speech subsisting in Him. Therefore, the attribute is necessary.
This is the crux of the proof: the description requires the attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن الكلام لفى الفؤاد وإنما جعل اللسان على الفؤاد دليلا وقال عمر رضى الله عنه : إنى زورت في نفسي مقالة وكثيرا ما تقول لصاحبك : إن فى نفسى كلاما أريد أن أذكره لك . والدليل على ثبوت صفة الكلام : إجماع الأمة وتواتر النقل عن الانبياء - عليهم السلام - أنه تعالى متكلم، مع القطع باستحالة التكلم من غير ثبوت صفة الكلام . فثبت : ان الله تعالى صفات ثمانية : هى : العلم والقدرة، والحياة ،والسمع والبصر، والإرادة والتكوين والكلام ولما كان في الثلاثة الأخيرة زيادة نزاع وخفاء، كرر الإشارة إلى إثباتها وقدمها .
Verily speech is in the heart, but the tongue is made a proof for the heart. And Umar, may God be pleased with him, said: I have prepared in myself a statement, and often you say to your companion: I have in myself speech that I want to mention to you. The proof for the establishment of the attribute of speech is: the consensus of the community and the uninterrupted transmission from the prophets, peace be upon them, that the Exalted is speaking, along with the certainty of the impossibility of speaking without the establishment of the attribute of speech. So it is established that God the Exalted has eight attributes: they are: knowledge, power, life, hearing, sight, will, creative power, and speech. And since there was additional dispute and obscurity concerning the last three, he repeated the indication of their proof and gave them precedence.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage provides the formal proof for the divine attribute of speech (kalam). It begins by citing evidence that speech is an internal reality in the heart, quoting a poetic verse and a statement of Umar. Then it presents the logical proof: the consensus of the Muslim community and the uninterrupted transmission from the prophets establish that God speaks (mutakallim). But it is impossible to describe God as speaking if the attribute of speech does not subsist in Him. Therefore, speech must be a real attribute of God. From this and other evidence, it is concluded that God has eight essential attributes: knowledge, power, life, hearing, sight, will, creative power (takwin), and speech. The author notes that the last three (will, takwin, speech) required more discussion due to greater dispute and subtlety, so the proof for them is repeated and given precedence.

Key Terms
الكلام
الصفات
إجماع
تواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that God's speech is merely a metaphorical or created entity, not a real attribute subsisting in His essence.
Correction: The passage argues that if God is described as speaking, the description must correspond to a real attribute; otherwise, the description would be false or impossible.

Checkpoint

B) Consensus of the community and uninterrupted transmission from prophets
C) Quranic verses and linguistic analysis
D) The saying of Umar and the poetic line

Key Takeaway
The divine attribute of speech is proven by the consensus and uninterrupted transmission that God speaks, and the logical necessity that the description implies a real attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

This lesson proves God's speech by consensus and logical necessity. Do you feel the weight of the consensus of the prophets and the community? How does that affect your certainty in this attribute? Will you now reflect on the Qur'an as the manifestation of that attribute?

The Eight Essential Attributes of Allah
The author lists the eight essential attributes and notes the special emphasis on the last three.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight essential attributes of Allah and understand why the last three require special emphasis.

Core Idea
Allah has eight essential attributes; the last three are most subtle and contested.

After establishing the attribute of speech, the author concludes that God has eight essential attributes. He notes that the last three—will, creative power (takwin), and speech—are more disputed and obscure, so their proofs are repeated and given precedence. This lesson will help you memorize the list and appreciate the author's pedagogical choice.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of eight attributes
Read the Arabic sentence that begins 'فثبت : ان الله تعالى صفات ثمانية'. Identify each attribute in order: knowledge, power, life, hearing, sight, will, creative power, and speech.
Notice that speech appears again as the last attribute, having just been proven.
2
Note the comment about the last three
Read the final sentence: 'ولما كان في الثلاثة الأخيرة زيادة نزاع وخفاء، كرر الإشارة إلى إثباتها وقدمها'. Understand that the author says these three had more dispute and were more hidden, so he repeated their proofs and gave them priority in the discussion.
This indicates the author's method: he addresses the most problematic attributes first.
3
Reflect on why these three are contested
Consider why will, creative power, and speech might be more controversial compared to knowledge, power, life, hearing, and sight. Think about how they relate to actions and human language.
This is a deeper theological point; the commentary will help.

The Eternal Nature of Divine Speech: Beyond Letters and Sounds
The author defines God's speech as an eternal attribute, not composed of letters/sounds, refuting Mu'tazila, Hanabila, and Karramiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine speech must be an eternal attribute, not composed of letters or sounds, and how this refutes key theological sects.

Core Idea
Divine speech is not like our speech; it is an eternal, non-composite attribute.

The nature of God's speech has been a major point of contention in Islamic theology. This passage from the creed clarifies that God's attribute of speech is eternal and not made up of letters or sounds, thereby refuting the positions of the Mu'tazila, Hanabila, and Karramiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the compact style and the use of 'ضرورة' (necessarily).
2
Understand the definition of 'speaking'
The author argues that to call God 'speaking', speech must be an attribute subsisting in Him. Grasp why this is necessary: you cannot derive a word from something that does not exist in the subject.
This directly refutes the Mu'tazila who say God's speech is created and subsists in something else.
3
Grasp the proof of eternity
The passage then states that speech is eternal because contingent things cannot subsist in God's essence. Reflect on the impossibility of God having changing attributes.
4
Analyze why speech is not letters/sounds
The author argues that letters and sounds are contingent accidents that require succession (one after another), so they cannot be eternal. See the self-evident impossibility of speaking a second letter without the first ending.
This refutes the Hanabila and Karramiyya who claim God's speech is composed of letters/sounds yet eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو أى الله تعالى متكلم بكلام ، هو صفة له ضرورة : امتناع إثبات المشتق للشيء من غير قيام ماخذ الاشتقاق به. وفى هذا رد على المعتزلة، حيث ذهبوا إلى أنه متكلم بكلام هو قائم بغيره، ليس صفة له . أزلية ضرورة امتناع قيام الحوادث بذاته . ليس من جنس الحروف والأصوات ضرورة أنها أعراض حادثة مشروط حدوث بعضها بانقضاء البعض، لأن امتناع التكلم بالحرف الثاني بدون انقضاء الحرف الأول بديهى. وفى هذا رد على الحنابلة والكرامية القائلين بأن كلامه تعالى عرض من جنس الأصوات والحروف، ومع ذلك فهو قديم .
And He, i.e., God the Exalted, is speaking with a speech that is an attribute of His, necessarily: because it is impossible to affirm a derived word for something without the source of the derivation subsisting in it. And in this is a refutation of the Mu'tazila, who held that He is speaking with a speech that subsists in something else, not an attribute of His. It is eternal, necessarily, because of the impossibility of contingent things subsisting in His essence. It is not of the genus of letters and sounds because they are contingent accidents, the occurrence of some of them conditioned upon the passing of others, for the impossibility of speaking a second letter without the passing of the first is self-evident. And in this is a refutation of the Hanabila and the Karramiyya, who hold that His speech is an accident of the genus of sounds and letters, yet it is eternal.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage explains the nature of God's attribute of speech. It begins by asserting that God is speaking (mutakallim) with a speech that is His attribute (sifa), because you cannot call something 'speaking' if the source of the derivation (speech) does not exist within it. This refutes the Mu'tazila, who say God's speech is created and subsists in something else (like the Preserved Tablet). Next, the author states that this speech is eternal (azaliyya), because contingent things (hawadith) cannot subsist in God's essence. Furthermore, it is not composed of letters and sounds (huruf wa aswat), because these are contingent accidents that require succession—one letter cannot occur before the previous one ends, which is self-evident. This refutes the Hanabila and Karramiyya, who claim God's speech is an accident consisting of letters and sounds, yet they also claim it is eternal. The argument is that if it were letters, it would be contingent and thus cannot be eternal.

Key Terms
متكلم
أزلية
حروف
أصوات
أعراض
حادثة
معتزلة
حنابلة
كرامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's speech is audible or composed of letters, like human speech.
Correction: God's speech is an eternal, non-composite attribute; it is not letters or sounds, which are contingent and sequential.

Checkpoint

A) Because letters are physical and God is not
B) Because letters are accidents that require succession, implying contingency
C) Because letters are created
D) Because God cannot speak in letters

Key Takeaway
Divine speech is an eternal, non-composite attribute, not composed of letters or sounds, transcending the limitations of created speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Divine Speech: One Attribute, Multiple Relations
The author explains divine speech as one attribute with multiple relations, answering an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine speech is a single eternal attribute that manifests as command, prohibition, and information through different relations, and why this understanding preserves tawhid.

Core Idea
God's speech is one; its diversity comes from relation, not essence.

This lesson addresses a subtle but crucial point in Islamic theology: how can one divine attribute produce different kinds of speech? The author explains that speech is a single attribute that becomes command, prohibition, or information by relating to different objects, just like knowledge and power. This avoids attributing multiplicity to God's essence while accounting for the variety of revealed speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the key terms: أمر, نهي, خبر, تعلق.
2
Identify the analogy
The author compares speech to other attributes like knowledge and power. How does this analogy help explain that speech is one attribute with many relations?
Knowledge is one attribute but relates to many objects; similarly, speech is one but relates to commands, prohibitions, etc.
3
Examine the objection and answer
Find the objection: 'These are divisions of speech, speech cannot be conceived without them.' Then see how the author responds. What is the key distinction he makes?
The answer hinges on the difference between eternity (azal) and time (fima la yazal).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والله تعالى متكلم بها آمر ناه مخبر يعنى أنه صفة واحدة تتكثر إلى الأمر والنهى والخبر باختلاف التعلقات كالعلم والقدرة وسائر الصفات . فإن كلا منها صفة واحدة قديمة، والتكثر والحدوث إنما هو فى التعلق والإضافات لما أن ذلك اليق بكمال التوحيد، ولأنه لا دليل على تكثر كل منها في نفسها فإن قيل : هذه أقسام للكلام لا يعقل وجوده بدونها . قلنا : إنه ممنوع، بل إنما يصير أحد تلك الأقسام عند التعلقات وذلك فيما لا يزال . وأما فى الأزل فلا انقسام أصلا. وذهب بعضهم : إلى أنه فى الأزل خبر ومرجع الكل إليه . لأن
And God the Exalted is speaking with it, commanding, prohibiting, informing, meaning that it is one attribute that multiplies into command, prohibition, and information according to the difference of relations, like knowledge, power, and the rest of the attributes. For each of them is one eternal attribute, and multiplicity and contingency are only in relation and relational aspects, because that is more fitting for the perfection of tawhid, and because there is no proof for the multiplicity of each in itself. If it is said: These are divisions of speech, speech cannot be conceived without them. We say: It is denied; rather, it becomes one of those divisions only upon relations, and that is in what is not yet. But in eternity there is no division at all. And some held that in eternity it is information, and the reference of all is to it. Because...
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage discusses the unity of the divine attribute of speech. It states that God speaks with one speech (sifa wahida) that becomes command (amr), prohibition (nahy), and information (khabar) according to different relations (ta'alliqat). This is likened to other attributes like knowledge and power, which are single eternal attributes but relate to many objects. Multiplicity and temporality (huduth) occur only in the relations, not in the essence of the attribute, because that is more fitting for the perfection of tawhid (monotheism) and because there is no evidence for multiplicity within the attribute itself. An objection is raised: command, prohibition, and information are essential divisions of speech; speech cannot be conceived without them. The author answers: this is denied; rather, speech only becomes one of these divisions when it relates to something, and that is in time (fima la yazal). In eternity (azal), there is no division at all. Finally, the author notes that some held that in eternity, speech is purely information (khabar), and all reference is to it—but the passage cuts off with 'because' (li'anna).

Key Terms
الأمر
النهي
الخبر
التعلق
التكثر
الإضافات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God has separate attributes for command, prohibition, and information.
Correction: These are manifestations of one single attribute (speech) through different relations, not separate attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the author, when does divine speech become command, prohibition, or information?
A) In eternity
B) Only in relation to creation, in time
C) Both in eternity and time
D) Only in the afterlife

Key Takeaway
Divine speech is one eternal attribute that becomes diverse only through relation, preserving divine simplicity and tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's speech is one and only becomes command or prohibition in relation to you, does your response to His commands reflect that you are encountering the very same eternal speech that He speaks? How does this truth weigh on your heart when you consider your obedience or negligence?
?
The author says multiplicity in speech is only in relation, not in essence. When you hear the Quran's commands, do you treat them as temporary or relational, or as flowing from God's one eternal attribute? How does this change the urgency with which you respond?
?
If in eternity there is no division in God's speech, then His command and prohibition are not separate from His essence. How does this reality affect your understanding of His perfect unity, and does it provoke you to seek a deeper, more unified devotion in your own life?
