Takwin: A Real Attribute, Not a Mere Relation
Defines Takwin and argues against its identification with the relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Takwin as a real attribute and why it cannot be reduced to the relation of bringing into existence.

Core Idea
Takwin is the source of creation, not merely the relation of bringing forth.

The author begins by defining Takwin precisely: it is a real attribute of Allah, the origin of the creative relation, but not the relation itself. This distinction is crucial because confusing the two leads to absurd conclusions about Allah's eternal act and its relationship to temporal effects.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the key terms: takwin, iḍāfa, mukawwan.
2
Identify the definition structure
Find where the author defines Takwin as a real attribute and the origin of the relation. Note that he explicitly says it is not the relation itself.
3
Examine the counterexample
The passage discusses the analogy of temporal striking (ḍarb). Ask yourself why the author rejects this analogy for Allah's act.
Divine action is eternal and does not require the effect to be simultaneous.
4
Understand the consequence
If Takwin were the relation, claiming it exists without the effect would be obstinacy. Grasp why this is self-evident according to the author.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتكوين صفة حقيقية هي مبدأ الإضافة التي هي إخراج المعدوم من العدم إلى الوجود، لا عينها. حتى لو كانت عينها على ما وقع في عبارة المشايخ، لكان القول بتحققها بدون المكون مكابرة وإنكارا للضرورى فلا يندفع بما يقال من أن الضرب عرض مستحيل البقاء، فلا بد لتعلقه بالمفعول ووصول الألم إليه من وجود المفعول. معه إذ لو تأخر لانعدم، وهو بخلاف فعل الباري، فإنه أزلى واجب الدوام، يبقى إلى وقت وجود المفعول . وهو غير المكون عندنا لأن الفعل يغاير المفعول بالضرورة كالضرب مع المضروب والأكل مع المأكول، ولأنه لو كان نفس المكون لزم أن يكون المكون مكونا مخلوقا بنفسه، ضرورة أنه مكون بالتكوين، الذي هو عينه فيكون قديما مستغنيا عن الصانع، وهو محال . وأن لا يكون للخالق تعلق بالعالم، سوى أنه أقدم منه وقادر عليه من غير صنع وتأثير في ضرورة تكونه بنفسه. وهذا لا يوجب كونه خالقا . والعالم مخلوقات له فلا يصح القول بأنه ليس خالق العالم وصانعه . هذا خلف. وأن لا يكون الله تعالى مكونا للأشياء، ضرورة أنه لا معنى للمكون إلا من قام به التكوين والتكوين إذا كان غير المكون لا يكون قائما بذات الله تعالى، وأن يصح القول بأن خالق سواد هذا الحجر أسود. وهذا الحجر خالق السواد. إذ لا معنى للخالق والأسود إلا من قام به الخلق ،والسواد وهما واحد، ومحلهما واحد وهذا كله تنبيه على كون الحكم بتغاير الفعل والمفعول ضروريا.
And Takwin (bringing into existence) is a real attribute (ṣifa ḥaqīqiyya) which is the origin of the relation (al-iḍāfa) that is bringing the non-existent from non-existence into existence, not the relation itself. So much so that if it were identical to it, as occurred in the expression of the shaykhs, then the statement that it is realized without the thing brought into existence (mukawwan) would be obstinacy and denial of the self-evident, and it cannot be repelled by what is said that striking (ḍarb) is an accident impossible to persist, so its attachment to the effect and the arrival of pain to it necessarily requires the existence of the effect with it, because if it were delayed it would cease to exist, and this is unlike the act of the Creator, for it is eternal (azalī) and necessarily perpetual, remaining until the time of the existence of the effect. And it (takwin) is not the thing brought into existence (mukawwan) according to us, because the act (fi‘l) is different from the effect (maf‘ūl) by necessity, like striking with the struck and eating with the eaten, and because if it were the same as the thing brought into existence, it would necessitate that the thing brought into existence be a creator (mukawwin) created by itself, necessarily because it is a thing brought into existence by takwin which is identical to it, so it would be eternal and independent of the Maker, and that is impossible. And that the Creator would have no attachment to the world except that He preceded it and is able over it without making or effect in the necessity of its coming into existence by itself. And this does not necessitate His being a creator. And the world is His creations, so it is not correct to say that He is not the creator and maker of the world. This is a contradiction. And that Allah Most High would not be the bringer into existence of things, necessarily because there is no meaning of 'bringer into existence' except the one in whom takwin subsists, and if takwin is other than the thing brought into existence, it does not subsist in the essence of Allah Most High; and that it would be correct to say that the creator of the blackness of this stone is black, and this stone is the creator of blackness. For there is no meaning of 'creator' and 'black' except the one in whom creation and blackness subsist, and they are one and their locus is one. And all of this is a reminder that the judgment of the difference between act and effect is necessary.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute takwin (bringing into existence) and proves that it is distinct from the mukawwan (the thing brought into existence). The author begins by stating that takwin is a real attribute (ṣifa ḥaqīqiyya) that is the source of the relation (iḍāfa) of bringing the non-existent from non-existence to existence, but it is not identical to that relation. He then argues that if it were identical, as some shaykhs have expressed, then claiming that takwin exists without the mukawwan would be obstinacy and denial of the self-evident. The counterexample of temporal striking (ḍarb) is rejected because divine action is eternal and does not require the effect to be simultaneous. The author then presents four absurd consequences of identifying takwin with mukawwan: (1) the mukawwan would be a creator of itself, hence eternal and independent of Allah; (2) the Creator would have no effective attachment to the world, only priority and power, which does not make Him a creator; (3) Allah would not be the bringer into existence of things, since the meaning of 'bringer into existence' requires that takwin subsist in Him, but if takwin is identical to the effect, it cannot subsist in Him; (4) it would be correct to say that the creator of blackness is black and that the stone is the creator of blackness, because both would share the same attribute. All these absurdities show that the judgment that act and effect are different is necessary.

Key Terms
التكوين (takwin)
الإضافة (al-iḍāfa)
المكون (mukawwan)
صفة حقيقية (ṣifa ḥaqīqiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Takwin is merely the relation of creation.
Correction: The author clarifies that Takwin is the source of the relation, not the relation itself.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what would happen if Takwin were identical to the relation of bringing into existence?
A) It would be an eternal attribute.
B) It would be realized without the effect.
C) It would be obstinacy and denial of the self-evident.
D) It would be like striking.

Key Takeaway
Takwin is a real attribute of Allah, the source of the creative relation, distinct from the relation itself and not dependent on the temporal existence of its effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your understanding of Allah's attribute of Takwin as a real, eternal attribute means that His act of creating is not a temporary event but flows from His essence. How does this change your perception of your own existence? Are you living as a mere 'effect' or as one constantly sustained by the Creator?
?
The passage distinguishes between the attribute and the relation. In your daily life, do you sometimes confuse your relationship with Allah (like the relation) with who He truly is (His attributes)? How can you move from focusing on your own experiences to truly knowing His eternal attributes?
?
If Takwin is an eternal attribute that does not require the existence of creation, then Allah's act of bringing you into existence is a free act of His will, not a necessity. What response does this truth demand from you right now, in terms of gratitude and submission?

The Necessary Distinction Between Act and Effect
Proves that Takwin is not identical to Mukawwan using the necessary difference between act and effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that Takwin is not identical to Mukawwan, based on the necessary distinction between act and effect.

Core Idea
Act and effect are necessarily distinct, just as striking differs from the struck.

Having defined Takwin, the author now provides a decisive argument: Takwin is not the same as Mukawwan because the act (fi‘l) is necessarily different from the effect (maf‘ūl). He illustrates with everyday examples and then shows the absurd consequences of conflating them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the analogy and the logical implication.
2
Analyze the analogy
The author uses examples like striking/struck and eating/eaten. Understand why these demonstrate the necessary difference between act and effect.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
If Takwin were identical to Mukawwan, then the Mukawwan would be a creator of itself and eternal. Grasp why this is impossible.
This shows the necessity of distinguishing Takwin from Mukawwan.

Source Text

Misconception: One might think that since Allah's act is eternal, it could be identical to its effect.

What does the author's analogy of striking and the struck illustrate?
A) That striking is an accident.
B) That act and effect are necessarily different.

The act of bringing into existence is necessarily distinct from the thing brought into existence, otherwise the creature would be self-creator and eternal.

?

?

?
The passage shows that even the most intimate acts (like eating) are distinct from their effects. How does this help you see Allah’s other attributes (like His knowledge or power) as distinct from the things He knows or empowers?

The Absurd Consequences of Identifying Takwin with Mukawwan
Lists three absurd consequences of identifying Takwin with Mukawwan, concluding that the distinction is necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three absurd consequences that follow from the false identification of Takwin with Mukawwan, reinforcing the necessity of their distinction.

Core Idea
If act and effect were one, the Creator would lose His effective role and creatures would become self-sufficient.

The author now drives home the point by exposing the unacceptable implications of conflating Takwin with its effect. These consequences show that such a view undermines the very meaning of creation and the Creator's relationship to the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the three consequences
Read the passage and identify the three absurd consequences listed. Use the translation to follow the logic.
2
Analyze each consequence
For each consequence, understand why it is absurd and how it violates basic theological principles.
The first consequence: Creator would have no effective attachment. The second: Allah would not be the bringer into existence. The third: creator of blackness would be black.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The author ends by saying these absurdities remind us that the distinction between act and effect is necessary. See how this conclusion ties back to the main argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the attribute of creation can be identical to the created thing.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the absurd consequences mentioned in the passage?
A) The Creator would have no effective attachment to the world.
B) Allah would not be the bringer into existence of things.
C) The creator of blackness would be black.
D) Takwin would be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The three absurd consequences prove that Takwin and Mukawwan must be distinct, preserving the Creator's effective role and the meaning of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God’s act of creation is completely distinct from the world, how would your view of secondary causes (like your own efforts) change? Are there areas where you act as if the world is self-sufficient, ignoring His effective role?
?
The third absurdity says it would be correct to call a stone the creator of blackness. In your daily life, do you ever attribute outcomes to people or circumstances as if they were independent creators? How can you redirect that attribution back to Allah in your speech and heart?
?
The passage argues that if Takwin were identical to Mukawwan, Allah would not be the bringer-into-existence. Reflect: do you sometimes feel you 'bring things into existence' by your own power? What practical steps can you take to affirm that He is the only true creator of every effect in your life?

The Importance of Charitable Interpretation in Scholarly Disputes
The author advises charitable interpretation before theological debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the methodological principle of interpreting statements of firmly rooted scholars in a sound manner before dismissing them as absurd.

Core Idea
Charitable interpretation is a prerequisite for sound theological debate.

Before delving into the technical discussion of takwin, the author pauses to warn against hasty conclusions. He advises that one should always seek a sound interpretation for the words of scholars, even when they seem problematic. This lesson establishes that intellectual charity is not mere politeness but a necessary condition for meaningful discourse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then the translation. Notice how the author addresses the reader directly as 'the intelligent person'.
2
Identify the two methodological commands
The author forbids attributing obvious absurdities to scholars and commands seeking a sound interpretation. Identify these in the text.
The command to seek a sound interpretation is the positive counterpart to the prohibition.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Why does the author begin with this advice? Consider how it sets the tone for the entire discussion of takwin and divine attributes.
This principle prevents misrepresenting the positions of earlier scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكنه ينبغي للعاقل أن يتأمل في أمثال هذه المباحث، ولا ينسب إلى الراسخين من علماء الأصول ما يكون استحالته بديهية ظاهرة على من له أدنى تمييز بل يطلب لكلامهم محملا صحيحا، يصلح محلا لنزاع العلماء، واختلاف العقلاء فإن من يقول : التكوين غير المكون أراد أن الفاعل إذا فعل شيئا فليس مهنا إلا الفاعل والمفعول . وأما المعنى الذى يعبر عنه بالتكوين والإيجاد، ونحو ذلك . فهو أمر اعتبارى يحصل في العقل من نسبة الفاعل إلى المفعول، وليس أمرا محققا مغايرا للمفعول في الخارج، ولم يرد أن مفهوم التكوين هو بعينه مفهوم المكون ليلزم المحالات. وهذا كما يقال : إن الوجود عين الماهية في الخارج، بمعنى أنه ليس فى الخارج للماهية تحقق ولعارضها المسمى بالوجود تحقق آخر حتى يجتمعا : القابل والمقبول، كالجسم ،والسواد، بل الماهية إذا كانت فتكونها هو وجودها، لكنهما متغايران في العقل، بمعنى أن للعقل أن يلاحظ الماهية دون الوجود .وبالعكس. فلا يتم إبطال هذا الرأى إلا بإثبات أن تكون الأشياء وصدورها عن البارى تعالى يتوقف على صفة حقيقية قائمة بالذات مغايرة للقدرة والإرادة . والتحقيق أن تعلق القدرة على وفق الإرادة بوجود المقدور لوقت وجوده إذا نسب إلى القدرة. يسمى إيجابا له، وإذا نسب إلى القادر يسمى الخلق والتكوين ونحو ذلك . فحقيقته كون الذات بحيث تعلقت قدرته بوجود المقدور لوقته، ثم يتحقق بحسب خصوصيات المقدورات خصوصيات الأفعال، كالترزيق والتصوير والإحياء والإماتة، وغير ذلك إلى ما لا يكاد يتناهى. وأما كون كل من ذلك صفة حقيقية أزلية، فمما انفرد به بعض علماء ما وراء النهر، وفيه تكثير للقدماء جدا، وإن لم تكن متغايرة .
But it is fitting for the intelligent person to reflect upon such inquiries, and not to attribute to the firmly rooted scholars of uṣūl (principles) what is obviously impossible to one with the least discernment. Rather, he should seek for their words a sound interpretation that can serve as a locus for scholarly debate and intellectual disagreement. For whoever says that takwin is other than mukawwan intends that when an agent does something, there is nothing there except the agent and the effect. As for the meaning expressed by takwin and ījād (bringing into existence) and the like, it is an intellectual consideration (amr i‘tibārī) that occurs in the mind from the relationship (nisba) of the agent to the effect, and it is not a real entity distinct from the effect in external existence (al-khārij). And he did not intend that the concept of takwin is identical to the concept of mukawwan, thereby entailing absurdities. This is like the saying that existence (wujūd) is identical to essence (māhiyya) in external existence, meaning that in external existence the essence does not have a realization and its accident called existence another realization such that the receiver and the received come together, like body and blackness. Rather, when the essence exists, its coming into existence is its existence, but they are distinct in the mind, meaning that the mind can observe the essence without existence and vice versa. So this view cannot be refuted except by proving that the coming into existence of things and their emanation from the Creator Most High depends on a real attribute subsisting in the essence, distinct from power (qudra) and will (irāda). And the verified truth (al-taḥqīq) is that the attachment of power in accordance with will to the existence of the thing willed (maqdūr) at the time of its existence, when attributed to power, is called ījāb (obligation) for it, and when attributed to the powerful (al-qādir), is called khalq (creation) and takwin and the like. So its reality is that the essence is such that His power is attached to the existence of the thing willed at its time. Then, according to the specificities of the things willed, specific acts are realized, such as providing sustenance (tarzīq), forming (taṣwīr), giving life (iḥyāʾ), causing death (imāta), and others without end. As for each of these being a real eternal attribute, this is something that some scholars from beyond the river (Mā warāʾ al-nahr) have held exclusively, and in it there is a great multiplication of eternal things, even if they are not distinct.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage provides the correct interpretation of the statement 'takwin is other than mukawwan' and clarifies the nature of divine action. The author begins by advising the intelligent person to reflect charitably on such debates and not to accuse scholars of holding absurd positions. He explains that when one says 'takwin is other than mukawwan', what is meant is that in the external world (al-khārij) there is only the agent (fā‘il) and the effect (maf‘ūl); the term 'takwin' or 'ījād' refers to an intellectual consideration (amr i‘tibārī) that arises in the mind from the relation of the agent to the effect. It is not a real entity distinct from the effect. The author then draws an analogy with the relationship between existence (wujūd) and essence (māhiyya) in external reality: in the external world, existence is identical to essence in the sense that they are not two separate things, but the mind can distinguish them. Thus, the view that takwin is not a separate real attribute can only be refuted if one proves that things depend on a real attribute distinct from power and will. The author then presents the 'verified truth' (al-taḥqīq): the attachment of power (qudra) in accordance with will (irāda) to the existence of the effect at its time, when ascribed to power, is called 'ījāb' (obligation), and when ascribed to the power-holder (qādir), is called 'khalq' and 'takwin' and so on. The reality is that the essence is such that His power is attached to the existence of the effect at its time. Then, according to the specificities of the effects, specific acts are realized (e.g., providing sustenance, forming, giving life, causing death). Finally, the author notes that considering each of these specific acts as a real eternal attribute is a position unique to some scholars from Transoxiana (Mā warāʾ al-nahr), and it involves an excessive multiplication of eternal entities, even if they are not distinct from one another.

Key Terms
أمر اعتباري (amr iʿtibārī)
النسبة (nisba)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author advise the intelligent person to do when encountering statements of firmly rooted scholars?
A) Reject them immediately if they seem impossible.
B) Seek a sound interpretation that can serve as a locus for scholarly debate.
C) Accept them without question.
D) Attribute them to the scholars' ignorance.

Key Takeaway
Before evaluating a theological statement, one must first seek a sound interpretation that is plausible and allows for meaningful debate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a statement from a scholar that first appears problematic, do you rush to judge, or do you pause to reflect as this lesson commands? What habit must you break to obey this advice?
?
Think of a scholar whose views you have dismissed or criticized. Did you first seek a sound interpretation for their words? If not, what might you owe them now?
?
In a recent theological discussion, did you assume that disagreement implies the other person holds an obviously false view? How will you change your approach after this lesson?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
Takwin as an Intellectual Consideration
The author explains the meaning of 'takwin is other than mukawwan' and draws an analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct meaning of the statement 'takwin is other than mukawwan' and its analogy with the relationship between existence and essence.

Core Idea
Takwin is not a real separate entity but a mental relation.

One of the controversial statements in theology is that 'takwin is other than mukawwan'. This lesson unpacks what scholars actually meant by it. The author clarifies that takwin is merely an intellectual consideration arising from the agent-effect relationship, analogous to how existence and essence are identical in external reality but distinct in the mind. This understanding prevents attributing absurdities to theologians.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on takwin
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting how the author describes what is meant by 'takwin is other than mukawwan'.
The author uses the example of an agent and an effect to illustrate.
2
Understand the analogy with wujud and mahiyya
The author compares takwin and mukawwan to existence (wujud) and essence (mahiyya). In external reality, they are not separate; only in the mind are they distinguished.
This analogy is key to grasping the intellectual consideration concept.
3
Recognize the condition for refutation
The author states that the view (that takwin is an intellectual consideration) can only be refuted by proving a real attribute distinct from qudra and irada. Consider what this implies.
This sets up the next lesson on the verified truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that takwin is a separate real entity existing alongside the effect in the external world.
Correction: The author clarifies that takwin is an intellectual consideration (amr i‘tibārī) that occurs in the mind, not a real entity distinct from the effect in external existence.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the correct understanding of the term 'takwin'?
A) A real eternal attribute subsisting in the divine essence.
B) An intellectual consideration arising from the relation of agent to effect.
C) The same as the effect in external existence.
D) A specific act like giving life or causing death.

Key Takeaway
The statement 'takwin is other than mukawwan' does not posit a real separate entity; takwin is only a mental consideration derived from the agent-effect relationship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If takwin is merely a mental consideration, then your understanding of God creating the universe is a relationship you conceive in your mind. Does that make God's act of creation feel less 'real' to you? How does that affect your certainty that He is your Creator?
?
When you say 'Allah created the heavens and the earth,' are you picturing a separate 'act' of creation added to God? This lesson says there is only the Creator and the created. Can you let go of needing an intermediate 'thing' and trust that His mere willing suffices?
?
The analogy with existence and essence forces you to examine whether you have been treating God's attributes as independent 'things' rather than aspects of His perfect being. Are you willing to refine your theology so that you do not imagine God as composed of parts?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
The Verified Truth of Divine Action and the Multiplication of Eternal Attributes
The author presents the verified truth of divine action and critiques the multiplication of eternal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's verified position on divine action and why considering every specific act as a real eternal attribute leads to excessive multiplication.

Core Idea
Divine action is the attachment of power to effect at its time, not a myriad of eternal attributes.

After clarifying what takwin is not, the author presents the verified truth (al-taḥqīq) of divine action. He explains that the attachment of power in accordance with will to the existence of a thing at its time is what underlies all specific acts. This lesson also examines and critiques the view of scholars who multiply eternal attributes for each specific divine action.

Guided Path
1
Read the taḥqīq passage
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'wal-taḥqīq' (the verified truth). Note how the author describes the attachment of power and will.
The author distinguishes between attribution to power (ījāb) and attribution to the powerful (khalq/takwin).
2
Identify the specific acts
The author lists acts like tarzīq, taṣwīr, iḥyāʾ, imāta. Understand that these are all derived from the same fundamental attachment.
3
Critique the multiplication of attributes
The author mentions that some scholars from Transoxiana consider each act a real eternal attribute. He criticizes this as an excessive multiplication of eternal things.
Even if these attributes are not distinct from each other, the multiplication is problematic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that each specific divine act (like giving life or causing death) requires a separate eternal attribute in God.
Correction: The author teaches that all acts reduce to the single attachment of power in accordance with will; the specific names are based on the effects, not new attributes.

Checkpoint
What does the author call the attachment of power in accordance with will when attributed to the powerful (al-qādir)?
A) Ījāb
B) Khalq and takwin
C) Tarzīq
D) Imāta

Key Takeaway
The true reality of divine action is the single attachment of power in accordance with will; the multiplication of specific acts as eternal attributes is a needless excess.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you sometimes complicate your understanding of God’s actions by imagining multiple separate 'decrees' or 'attributes' in your mind? What passage from this lesson challenges you to simplify your belief?
?
The author warns against multiplying eternal things needlessly. In your own life, do you multiply unnecessary beliefs or practices that distract from the core reality of God’s power and will? What is one specific thing you can remove today?
?
When you reflect on the specific actions of God in your life (like provision, life, death), do you see them as separate from His single power, or as manifestations of it? How does this lesson invite you to change your perspective?

The Dispute over Takwin: Mental Consideration or Real Attribute?
The author explains the dispute over Takwin and presents the mental consideration view with an analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the position that Takwin is a mental consideration distinct from the created thing, and the analogy used to explain it.

Core Idea
Takwin is not a real entity but a mental relation between the Creator and creation.

The nature of divine creation has been debated by theologians. Some argue that the act of bringing into existence (takwin) is merely a mental concept derived from relating the Creator to the creature. This lesson examines that view and the analogy with existence and essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the gist of the argument.
Pay attention to the analogy.
2
Identify the two views
Notice the dispute: one view says Takwin is a real attribute, the other says it is a mental consideration.
3
Understand the analogy
The author compares Takwin to existence being identical to essence in the external world but distinct in the mind.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this view leads to the need for a real attribute later.
This prepares for the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محلا لنزاع العلماء، واختلاف العقلاء فإن من يقول : التكوين غير المكون أراد أن الفاعل إذا فعل شيئا فليس مهنا إلا الفاعل والمفعول . وأما المعنى الذى يعبر عنه بالتكوين والإيجاد، ونحو ذلك . فهو أمر اعتبارى يحصل في العقل من نسبة الفاعل إلى المفعول، وليس أمرا محققا مغايرا للمفعول في الخارج، ولم يرد أن مفهوم التكوين هو بعينه مفهوم المكون ليلزم المحالات. وهذا كما يقال : إن الوجود عين الماهية في الخارج، بمعنى أنه ليس فى الخارج للماهية تحقق ولعارضها المسمى بالوجود تحقق آخر حتى يجتمعا : القابل والمقبول، كالجسم ،والسواد، بل الماهية إذا كانت فتكونها هو وجودها، لكنهما متغايران في العقل، بمعنى أن للعقل أن يلاحظ الماهية دون الوجود .وبالعكس. فلا يتم إبطال هذا الرأى إلا بإثبات أن تكون الأشياء وصدورها عن البارى تعالى يتوقف على صفة حقيقية قائمة بالذات مغايرة للقدرة والإرادة . والتحقيق أن تعلق القدرة على وفق الإرادة بوجود المقدور لوقت وجوده إذا نسب إلى القدرة. يسمى إيجابا له، وإذا نسب إلى القادر يسمى الخلق والتكوين ونحو ذلك . فحقيقته كون الذات بحيث تعلقت قدرته بوجود المقدور لوقته، ثم يتحقق بحسب خصوصيات المقدورات خصوصيات الأفعال، كالترزيق والتصوير والإحياء والإماتة، وغير ذلك إلى ما لا يكاد يتناهى. وأما كون كل من ذلك صفة حقيقية أزلية، فمما انفرد به بعض علماء ما وراء النهر، وفيه تكثير للقدماء جدا، وإن لم تكن متغايرة . والأقرب ما ذهب إليه المحققون منهم، وهو أن مرجع الكل إلى التكوين. فإنه إن تعلق بالحياة يسمى إحياء، وبالموت إماتة، وبالصورة تصويرا، وبالرزق ترزيقا إلى غير ذلك. فالكل تكوين وإنما الخصوص بخصوص التعلقات .
It is a locus of dispute among scholars and disagreement among intellectuals. For he who says: Takwin (bringing into existence) is other than the created thing (al-mukawwan) intends that when the agent (al-fa'il) does something, there is nothing there except the agent and the acted-upon (al-maf'ul). As for the meaning expressed by takwin, creation (al-ijad), and the like, it is a mental consideration (amr i'tibari) that occurs in the mind from the relation of the agent to the acted-upon, and is not a real thing (amr muhaqqaq) distinct from the acted-upon in the external world. He did not intend that the concept of takwin is identical to the concept of the created thing so that absurdities would follow. This is like it is said: Existence (al-wujud) is identical to essence (al-mahiyya) in the external world, meaning that in the external world the essence does not have a realization and its accident called existence has another realization such that both the receptacle and the received would unite like a body and blackness. Rather, if the essence exists, its becoming-existence is its existence, but they are distinct in the mind, meaning that the mind can observe the essence without existence, and vice versa. This opinion cannot be refuted except by proving that the coming-to-be of things and their issuing from Allah the Exalted depends upon a real attribute (sifa haqiqiyya) subsisting in the Essence, distinct from power (al-qudra) and will (al-irada). The investigation (al-tahqiq) is that the relation of power in accordance with will to the existence of the object of power at the time of its existence, when attributed to power, is called bringing about (ijab) for it, and when attributed to the powerful agent, it is called creation (al-khalq) and bringing into being (al-takwin) and the like. Its reality is that the Essence is such that His power relates to the existence of the object of power at its time. Then according to the particularities of the objects of power, particularities of actions are realized, such as providing sustenance (al-tarziq), forming (al-taswir), giving life (al-ihya'), causing death (al-imata), and others beyond count. As for each of these being a real eternal attribute, that is uniquely held by some scholars of Transoxiana, and it involves a great multiplication of eternal things, even if they are not distinct. The closer view is what the verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun) among them hold: that all of them refer back to takwin. For if it relates to life it is called giving life, if to death causing death, if to form forming, if to sustenance providing sustenance, and so on. All is takwin, and the particularity is only by the particularity of the relations.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the attribute of Takwin (bringing into existence) and its relation to the created things. The author begins by stating that the issue of whether Takwin is distinct from the created thing is a subject of dispute. He explains the position of those who say Takwin is not other than the created thing: they argue that when an agent acts, there is only the agent and the acted-upon. The concept of 'bringing into existence' is merely a mental consideration arising from relating the agent to the act; it is not a real, distinct entity in the external world. The author parallels this with the identity of existence and essence in the external world: existence is not an additional accident but the actualization of the essence itself, though they are distinct in the mind. He then states that this opinion can only be refuted by proving that the origination of things depends on a real attribute distinct from power and will. The author then provides his own investigation (tahqiq): the relation of divine power, in accordance with will, to the existence of the object at its proper time, when attributed to power is called 'ijab' (bringing about), and when attributed to the agent is called 'khalq' (creation) and 'takwin'. The reality of takwin is that the divine essence is such that His power relates to the existence of the object at its time. Then, according to the specific objects of power, specific actions like providing sustenance, forming, etc., come to be. The author notes that some scholars from Transoxiana consider each of these specific actions to be a distinct eternal attribute, which multiplies eternal entities excessively, even if they are not distinct. The closer view, adopted by the verifiers among them, is that all these specific actions refer back to the single attribute of takwin. The particularity comes from the particularities of the relations (ta'alluqat) — e.g., if takwin relates to life, it is called giving life; if to death, causing death, etc. Thus, the essential attribute is takwin, and the multiplicity is only in the relations.

Key Terms
التكوين
المكون
الفاعل
المفعول
أمر اعتباري
الماهية
الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The view that Takwin is a mental consideration means that the concept of Takwin is identical to the concept of the created thing.
Correction: The author explicitly states that they do not intend identity; it is a mental consideration distinct from the created thing.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the view that Takwin is other than the created thing mean?
A) Takwin is a real eternal attribute.
B) Takwin is a mental consideration arising from the relation of agent to act.
C) Takwin is identical to the created thing.
D) Takwin is an attribute distinct from power and will.

Key Takeaway
Takwin, according to one view, is a mental consideration deriving from the relation between the Creator and creation, not a real attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Takwin is merely a mental consideration, does that make Allah's act of creation less real in your heart? How does understanding creation as an immediate relation between the Creator and you affect your sense of dependency on Him?
?
The passage says that in the external world, essence and existence are one. Consider your own existence: do you live as if your existence is separate from your essence, or do you recognize that your very being is directly from Allah? What changes today if you truly internalize that your existence is not an added accident but your very reality from Him?
?
When you contemplate Allah's attribute of 'bringing into existence', do you feel the awe of His immediate power, or do you think of it as a distant process? How can you cultivate a constant awareness that you are in every moment being brought into existence by Him?

The Investigation of Takwin: A Single Attribute with Multiple Relations
The author presents the investigation of Takwin, its reality as the relation of power, and the unity of all creative acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's investigation of Takwin as the relation of divine power and the conclusion that all specific creative acts are expressions of a single attribute.

Core Idea
All acts of creation are one attribute of Takwin, differing only by relation to their objects.

After presenting the dispute, the author now provides his own investigation. He argues that the coming-to-be of things requires a real attribute distinct from power and will. He then explains that Takwin is the relation of power to the object, and that specific acts like giving life or causing death are not separate attributes but the same Takwin related to different objects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to follow the logical progression from refuting the earlier view to the final synthesis.
2
Identify the investigative approach
Notice how the author first states the need for a real attribute, then defines Takwin as a relation.
3
Understand the specific actions
See how the particularities of objects produce different names for the same attribute.
4
Analyze the disagreement about multiplicity
Some scholars multiplied eternal attributes, but the author prefers the view of the verifiers.
5
Grasp the conclusion
All actions are reducible to Takwin, with differences only in relations.

The Attribute of Irada: Definition and Proofs
Sanusi defines Irada and refutes deviant sects with three proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Allah's attribute of Will (Irada) as an eternal attribute, the sects that deviated from it, and the three proofs that establish it.

Core Idea
Allah's will is an eternal attribute that specifies creation, not a necessity or a temporal accident.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary defines the divine attribute of Irada (Will) and refutes four incorrect views. It then provides three proofs: scriptural, teleological, and cosmological. Understanding this lays the foundation for grasping how Allah's actions are voluntary and purposeful.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: definition, refutation, proofs.
The author repeats the definition for emphasis.
2
Understand the definition of Irada
Identify that Irada is an eternal attribute subsisting in Allah's essence that specifies (takhsis) created things in a particular manner and time.
This refutes any notion of Allah being a necessary agent without will.
3
Identify the four deviant views
List the four sects mentioned: philosophers (necessary agent), an-Najjariyya (will by essence), some Mu'tazila (created will not in a locus), al-Karramiyya (created will in essence).
Each deviates from affirming a real, eternal attribute of will.
4
Analyze the three proofs
Examine each proof: 1) Quranic verses affirming will + principle that attribute subsists in attributable, 2) order and goodness of the world showing a free chooser, 3) temporal origination of the world implying a voluntary agent.
The third proof is a cosmological argument against necessary emanation.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this matters: it establishes that Allah acts by will and choice, not by blind necessity, preserving divine wisdom and purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإرادة صفة الله تعالى أزلية قائمة بذاته كرر ذلك تأكيدا وتحقيقا لإثبات صفة قديمة الله تعالى تقتضى تخصيص المكونات بوجه دون وجه في وقت دون وقت لا كما زعمت الفلاسفة من أنه تعالى موجب بالذات لا فاعل بالإرادة والاختيار والنّجارية من أنه مريد بذاته لا بصفته، وبعض المعتزلة من أنه مريد بإرادة حادثة لا في محل، والكرامية من أن إرادته حادثة في ذاته. والدليل على ما ذكرنا الآيات الناطقة بإثبات صفة الإرادة والمشيئة الله تعالى، مع القطع بلزوم قيام صفة الشيء به، وامتناع قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى. وأيضا نظام العالم ووجوده على الوجه الأوفق الأصلح دليل على كون صانعه قادرا مختارا. ( وكذا حدوثه ) إذ لو كان صانعه موجبا بالذات لزم قدمه ضرورة امتناع تخلف المعلوم عن علته الموجبة.
Will (al-irada) is an attribute of Allah the Exalted, eternal, subsisting in His Essence. He repeated this for emphasis and verification to affirm a pre-eternal attribute of Allah that necessitates the specification of originated things in one manner rather than another, at one time rather than another, not as the philosophers claimed that He is necessary by essence (mujib bi-dh-dhat), not an agent by will and choice, nor as an-Najjariyya claimed that He is willing by His essence not by an attribute, nor as some Mu'tazila claimed that He is willing by a temporally originated will not subsisting in a locus, nor as al-Karramiyya claimed that His will is temporally originated in His essence. The proof of what we have mentioned is the verses that speak of affirming the attribute of will and wish of Allah, along with the certainty of the necessity of an attribute's subsisting in what it is attributed to, and the impossibility of temporally originated things subsisting in His Essence. Also, the order of the world and its existence in the most fitting and most beneficial manner is evidence that its Maker is powerful and free-choosing (qadir mukhtar). And also its temporal origination (huduth), for if its Maker were necessary by essence, its pre-eternity (qidam) would be necessary due to the impossibility of the effect's delay from its necessary cause.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the attribute of Irada (Will) for Allah. The author begins by stating that Irada is an eternal attribute subsisting in the divine essence. He emphasizes this is repeated for confirmation. The function of Irada is to specify (takhsis) the originated things in a particular manner and time. This refutes several deviant views: the philosophers who say Allah is a necessary agent (mujib bi-dh-dhat) without will; an-Najjariyya who say He is willing by His essence not by an attribute; some Mu'tazila who say He is willing by a created will not in a locus; and al-Karramiyya who say His will is created in His essence. The author then provides proofs. First is scriptural: the Quranic verses that affirm the attributes of Irada and Mashiyya (will), combined with the rational principle that an attribute must subsist in the one it qualifies, and that temporal accidents cannot subsist in Allah's eternal essence. Second is rational: the order and existence of the world in the best and most fitting way proves the Maker is powerful and free-choosing (qadir mukhtar). Third, the temporal origination (huduth) of the world: if the Maker were a necessary cause, the world would be eternal, because the effect cannot be delayed from its sufficient cause. This argument refutes the philosophers' claim of necessary emanation.

صفة أزلية
تخصيص

فاعل بالاختيار
النجارية
المعتزلة
الكرامية
حدوث
قدم
قادر مختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's will is either identical to His essence (as an-Najjariyya claimed) or created (as some Mu'tazila and Karramiyya claimed).
Correction: The author affirms that Irada is an eternal attribute distinct from the essence, subsisting in it, and not temporally originated.

Checkpoint
Which sect held that Allah's will is temporally originated in His essence?
A) The philosophers
B) An-Najjariyya
C) Al-Karramiyya
D) Some Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
Allah's will is an eternal attribute that specifies creation, refuting determinism and temporal creation of will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that every single detail of your life—your trials, your blessings, the timing of events—is specifically willed by Allah, does that fill you with contentment or unrest? What does your heart reveal about your trust in His will?
?
If you truly believe that Allah's will is eternal and not subject to change, how does that affect your reaction when your plans fail or when you face unexpected hardships? Will you submit to His specification with patience and gratitude?
?
The philosophers argued that Allah's will is a necessary emanation, leaving no room for choice. In your own life, do you ever live as if your circumstances are mechanically inevitable, forgetting that the All-Willing could have decreed otherwise? How can you actively remind yourself of His free and wise will?

All Divine Acts Reduce to Takwin
The author states the position that all divine acts are rooted in takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the position that all specific divine acts are manifestations of a single attribute of takwin, differing only by attachment.

Core Idea
All divine acts are one: takwin, differing only by attachment.

This passage presents a key theological position that simplifies the multiplicity of divine acts into a single attribute. Before diving into details of each act, we need to grasp this unifying principle. The author cites the view of the 'investigators' among theologians, which is considered the closest to the truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice the structure: a claim, then conditional examples, then a conclusion.
The phrase 'إلى غير ذلك' indicates that the examples are not exhaustive.
2
Understand the main claim
The passage states that the reference of all divine acts is to takwin. This means takwin is the essential attribute behind every specific act.
Takwin is often translated as 'origination' or 'bringing into existence'.
3
Examine the examples
The text lists four examples: giving life, causing death, forming, and providing. Each is a particular application of takwin depending on what it is attached to.
Attachment (ta'alluq) means the relation of the attribute to its object.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The final sentence emphasizes that everything is takwin; the specific names come only from specific attachments. This resolves the multiplicity of divine acts into a single attribute.
This view simplifies the understanding of divine attributes and avoids positing multiple separate eternal attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأقرب ما ذهب إليه المحققون منهم، وهو أن مرجع الكل إلى التكوين. فإنه إن تعلق بالحياة يسمى إحياء، وبالموت إماتة، وبالصورة تصويرا، وبالرزق ترزيقا إلى غير ذلك. فالكل تكوين وإنما الخصوص بخصوص التعلقات.
And the closest [view] is what the investigators among them went to, which is that the reference of all [acts] is to takwin (origination). For if it is attached to life it is called giving life, and to death causing death, and to form forming, and to provision providing, and so on. So all is takwin, and particularity is only due to particular attachments.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal clarification about the divine attribute of takwin. The author states the view of the 'investigators' (al-muhaqqiqun) among the theologians: all specific divine acts (like giving life, causing death, forming, providing) are in reality the single attribute of takwin (origination). The different names arise only because of the different objects (tacalluqat) to which this attribute is attached. Thus, the essential act is one, and diversity comes from the relata.

تعلق

إماتة
تصوير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: That God has multiple distinct creative attributes rather than a single attribute of origination with multiple effects.
Correction: The passage teaches that all specific divine acts (giving life, causing death, etc.) are not separate attributes but are the single attribute of takwin, differing only by the object to which it is attached.

Checkpoint

C) They are temporal events
D) They are metaphorical expressions

Key Takeaway
All divine acts are essentially one attribute of takwin, differing only in their attachments.

Definition and Proof of the Divine Will
The author defines al-Irada as an eternal attribute and provides scriptural and rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the divine will as an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence, the refutation of deviant views, and the scriptural and rational proofs for it.

Core Idea
God's will is eternal and necessitates the particularization of all things.

This lesson addresses a central attribute of Allah: al-Irada (will). The author begins by defining it as an eternal attribute that subsists in God's essence and explains its function of particularizing created things in specific ways and times. He then refutes several incorrect understandings held by various groups, and finally provides both scriptural and rational evidence to establish this attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of al-Irada
Read the opening sentence carefully. Note that the author emphasizes the eternity of the attribute. Understand that will involves particularization (takhsis).
2
Identify the refuted views
The text refutes four groups: philosophers, an-Najjariyya, some Mu'tazila, and the Karamiyya. For each, note what they wrongly claim about God's will.
This shows the importance of correct Aqeedah.
3
Examine the proofs
Two proofs are given: Qur'anic verses combined with logical principles, and the order of the world. Reflect on how these support the definition.
The rational proof from design is a common argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإرادة صفة الله تعالى أزلية قائمة بذاته كرر ذلك تأكيدا وتحقيقا لإثبات صفة قديمة لله تعالى تقتضى تخصيص المكونات بوجه دون وجه في وقت دون وقت لا كما زعمت الفلاسفة من أنه تعالى موجب بالذات لا فاعل بالإرادة والاختيار والنجارية من أنه مريد بذاته لا بصفته، وبعض المعتزلة من أنه مريد بإرادة حادثة لا في محل والكرامية من أن إرادته حادثة في ذاته. والدليل على ما ذكرنا الآيات الناطقة بإثبات صفة الإرادة والمشيئة لله تعالى، مع القطع بلزوم قيام صفة الشيء به، وامتناع قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى. وأيضا نظام العالم ووجوده على الوجه الأوفق الأصلح دليل على كون صانعه قادرا مختارا.
And the will is an attribute of God Most High, eternal, subsisting in His essence. He repeated that as emphasis and verification to establish an eternal attribute of God Most High that necessitates the particularization of originated things in one manner rather than another and in one time rather than another, not as the philosophers claimed that He is necessary by essence, not an agent by will and choice, and an-Najjariyya that He is willing by essence not by an attribute, and some Mu'tazila that He is willing by a temporal will not in a locus, and the Karamiyya that His will is temporal in His essence. And the evidence for what we mentioned is the verses that speak of establishing the attribute of will and volition for God Most High, together with the certainty of the necessity of an attribute of a thing subsisting in it, and the impossibility of temporal events subsisting in His essence. Also, the order of the world and its existence in the most suitable and most beneficial manner is evidence that its Maker is powerful and chooser.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of al-Irada (will). The author states that will is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence. It entails particularization (takhsis) of created things in specific ways and times. The author then refutes several deviant views: the philosophers say God is a necessary cause (mujib bi-dhat) not an agent by will; an-Najjariyya say He wills by essence not by an attribute; some Mu'tazila say He wills by a temporal will not in a locus; the Karamiyya say His will is temporal in His essence. The proof is twofold: (1) Qur'anic verses affirming will and volition, combined with the principle that an attribute must subsist in the one described and that temporal events cannot subsist in God's essence; (2) the order and optimal design of the world proves the Maker is powerful and free-choosing.

Key Terms

تخصيص (particularization)
موجب بالذات (necessary by essence)
مريد (willing)
مشيئة (volition)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's will is temporal or not an attribute subsisting in His essence, for example, the view of the Karamiyya.
Correction: God's will is eternal and subsists in His essence. It is not a temporal event.

Checkpoint

B) It necessitates particularization of created things
C) It is a temporal event
D) It is not an attribute

Key Takeaway
God's will is an eternal attribute that particularizes all created things, as proven by scripture and the design of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Some philosophers reduce God to a necessary cause, stripping Him of will. Is there an area in your worship where you treat God like a predictable machine—performing rituals without expecting personal, willed response from Him? Definition of ru'yah (vision of God)
The author defines ru'yah as complete disclosure by the sense of sight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of ru'yah (vision of God) as complete disclosure by the sense of sight, and how it differs from mere intellectual knowledge.

Core Idea
Ru'yah is a distinct perceptual state of complete disclosure by sight, not just intellectual cognition.

In this passage, al-Nasafi provides a technical definition of ru'yah, the vision of God, a key attribute debated in kalam. He clarifies that vision is not mere knowledge but a special state of complete disclosure by the sense of sight. The moon analogy illustrates the difference between knowing something and actually seeing it.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Notice the precise phrasing al-Nasafi uses.
2
Identify the definition of ru'yah
Find the two key phrases: 'complete disclosure by sight' (الانكشاف التام بالبصر) and 'perceiving a thing as it is by the sense of sight' (إدراك الشيء كما هو بحاسة البصر). Write them down.
3
Analyze the moon analogy
Consider the example of looking at the full moon then closing your eyes. Why is the state with open eyes called 'vision' while the state with closed eyes is not?
The author emphasizes that disclosure is more complete when the eyes are open, and this special state is what we call vision.
4
Distinguish ru'yah from intellectual knowledge
Reflect on how ru'yah is different from simply knowing about an object. The analogy shows that even when eyes are closed, you still have knowledge of the moon, but not vision.
5
Reflect on theological significance
Think about why defining ru'yah precisely matters for debates about seeing God in the afterlife. How does this definition support the possibility of vision?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورؤية الله تعالى بمعنى الانكشاف التام بالبصر، وهو معنى إدراك الشيء كما هو بحاسة البصر. وذلك أنا إذا نظرنا إلى البدر، ثم غمضنا العين، فلا خفاء في أنه وإن كان منكشفاً لدينا في الحالين، لكن انكشافه حال النظر إليه أتم وأكمل، ولنا بالنسبة إليه حينئذ حالة مخصوصة، هي المسماة بالرؤية.
And the vision of God Most High means complete disclosure by sight, and it is the meaning of perceiving a thing as it is by the sense of sight. And that is because if we look at the full moon, then close our eyes, there is no doubt that although it is disclosed to us in both states, still its disclosure at the time of looking at it is more complete and perfect, and we have in relation to it at that time a particular state, which is called vision.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage defines ru'yah (vision of God). The author explains it as 'complete disclosure (inkishaf) by sight' and 'perceiving a thing as it is by the sense of sight'. He illustrates with an analogy: when we look at the full moon and then close our eyes, the moon is known in both states, but the state when the eyes are open is a special, more perfect disclosure. That state is called vision. Thus ru'yah is not mere intellectual cognition but a distinct perceptual state.

Key Terms
رؤية (vision)
انكشاف (disclosure)
بصر (sight)
إدراك (perception)
حاسة (sense)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ru'yah is just intellectual knowledge or a metaphor.
Correction: Ru'yah is a distinct perceptual state of complete disclosure by the sense of sight, as clarified by the moon analogy which shows it is more than mere knowledge.

Checkpoint
What is the defining characteristic of ru'yah according to the author?
A) It is intellectual knowledge
B) It is complete disclosure by sight
C) It is a metaphor for understanding
D) It is only possible in dreams

Key Takeaway
Ru'yah is the complete disclosure of an object by the sense of sight, a special perceptual state beyond mere knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know Allah exists intellectually, but do you see Him with the eye of your heart? When you recite His names, do you merely know them, or do they unveil His majesty as if you witness Him? What habit would you change to turn your knowledge into vision?
?
The moon analogy shows that vision is a more complete disclosure than mere knowledge. In your relationship with Allah, have you settled for 'eyes closed' faith—knowing about Him without truly experiencing His presence? What step will you take this week to seek that deeper disclosure?
?
If ru'yah is the most perfect perception, are you living as if you are already seeing Allah? The Prophet ﷺ said, 'Worship Allah as if you see Him.' What is the one distraction that prevents you from that state, and how will you remove it starting today?

Definition of Ru'ya and Its Rational Possibility
Defines ru'ya and states its rational possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of ru'ya as complete disclosure by sight and its rational possibility, as well as the burden of proof for claims of impossibility.

Core Idea
Ru'ya is rationally possible unless proven otherwise—the default is permissibility.

Before discussing whether Allah can be seen in the afterlife, we need a clear definition of what ru'ya means. The author begins by defining ru'ya as complete disclosure through the sense of sight and gives a helpful example of looking at the moon. He then establishes that reason alone does not judge it impossible; rather, the burden of proof lies on those who deny it. This foundational clarity is essential for the theological debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation to get the full flow of the argument.
Notice the author's precise phrasing.
2
Identify the definition and the rational claim
Notice how the author first defines ru'ya, then provides an analogy, and finally states the rational principle.
The example of the moon illustrates the difference between mere knowledge and vision.
3
Understand the burden of proof
Reflect on what it means for something to be 'permissible in reason'—that it is not impossible unless proof shows otherwise.
Think about how this principle is used in later theological arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورؤية الله تعالى بمعنى الانكشاف التام بالبصر، وهو معنى إدراك الشيء كما هو بحاسة البصر . وذلك أنا إذا نظرنا إلى البدر، ثم غمضنا العين، فلا خفاء في أنه وإن كان منكشفاً لدينا في الحالين، لكن انكشافه حال النظر إليه أتم وأكمل، ولنا بالنسبة إليه حينئذ حالة مخصوصة، هي المسماة بالرؤية . جائزة فى العقل بمعنى أن العقل إذا خلى ونفسه لم يحكم بامتناع رؤيته، ما لم يقم له برهان على مانع على ذلك مع أن الأصل عدمه. وهذا القدر ضرورى . فمن ادعى الامتناع فعليه البيان .
And seeing Allah, the Exalted, means complete disclosure by sight, and it is the meaning of perceiving something as it is through the sense of sight. That is because when we look at the full moon, then close our eyes, there is no doubt that although it is disclosed to us in both states, its disclosure when looking is more complete and perfect, and for us relative to it at that time there is a specific state which is called ru'ya. It is permissible in reason, meaning that reason, if left to itself, does not judge the impossibility of seeing Him, as long as no proof of an obstacle to that is established, while the original principle is its absence. And this much is necessary. So whoever claims impossibility must provide the proof.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage defines the term ru'ya (seeing Allah) and establishes its rational possibility. The author begins by explaining that ru'ya means 'complete disclosure through the sense of sight,' i.e., perceiving something as it is with the eye. He provides an example: when we look at the full moon and then close our eyes, the moon is still known to us in both states, but the disclosure when looking is more complete and perfect. That special state is called ru'ya. He then states that ru'ya is rationally possible ('ja'iza fi al-'aql'), meaning that reason does not automatically judge it impossible; rather, one must bring a proof that it is impossible. The default principle is that it is not impossible. Therefore, whoever claims impossibility bears the burden of proof.

Key Terms
رؤية
انكشاف تام
بصر
جواز عقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that ru'ya means seeing Allah as we see physical objects with the same modality.
Correction: Ru'ya is defined as complete disclosure by the sense of sight, not necessarily identical to our physical vision of material things. The passage focuses on the concept of disclosure, not the mechanics.

Checkpoint
What does ru'ya mean according to the passage?
A) Knowing Allah's essence
B) Complete disclosure through the sense of sight
C) Intellectual perception
D) Vision in dreams

Key Takeaway
Ru'ya is defined as complete disclosure by sight and is rationally possible unless a valid objection is proven.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author uses the example of the moon to illustrate that our experience of sight is more than just 'knowing'—it is a distinct state of complete disclosure. When you think about the Day of Judgment and the vision of Allah, do you truly long for that complete, unveiled encounter? Or are you content with merely knowing about Him? What is blocking that yearning in your heart?
?
Reason alone does not forbid seeing Allah—so why do you sometimes act as if Allah is distant or hidden? Is your disbelief or doubt in the possibility of drawing near to Allah based on your own rational limitations, or on a lack of spiritual desire? What would it take for you to sincerely hope for the beatific vision?
?
If someone were to claim that seeing Allah is impossible, the passage says the burden of proof is on them. But in your own life, do you place burdens on Allah by assuming certain ways He must act? Have you ever demanded proof from Him while ignoring the proofs He has given? Reflect: Are you open to what Allah might reveal, or do you let your own assumptions close the door to deeper faith?

Answer to Scriptural Objection from Quran 6:103
Interpretation of Quran 6:103 and its scope regarding vision of Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse 'لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ' is interpreted to allow the vision of Allah in the afterlife, based on the distinctions between 'عموم السلب' and 'سلب العموم' and the limitation of the verse's scope to times and states.

Core Idea
The verse denies comprehensive grasp, not all vision, and not for all times.

One of the key scriptural objections to the Sunni belief in the vision of Allah in the afterlife is the Quranic verse 'No vision can grasp Him.' In this passage, the commentator provides a nuanced answer that distinguishes between different types of negation and the scope of the verse. By examining the language and context, he shows that the verse does not preclude vision in the Hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the verse and the author's answer.
Pay attention to the distinction between 'عموم السلب' and 'سلب العموم'.
2
Understand the linguistic distinction
The author concedes that 'الأبصار' is generic, but clarifies that the verse indicates 'عموم السلب' (universal negation) not 'سلب العموم' (negation of universality). Grasp what each means in context.
عموم السلب: negation applies to every individual. سلب العموم: negation of every individual (stronger).
3
Define 'إدراك' as encompassing vision
The author defines 'إدراك' in this context as vision that encompasses the sides of the visible object, not mere vision. This limits the denial to comprehensive grasp.
Thus the verse denies anyone can 'encompass' Allah in vision, not simply see Him.
4
Limit the verse to times and states
Finally, the author argues that even with these concessions, the verse does not indicate that vision is impossible at all times and states—only perhaps in this world or in a specific manner.
This opens the door for the afterlife vision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن السمعيات قوله تعالى : وَلا تُدْرِكُهُ الأَبْصَارُ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الأَبْصَارَ [الأنعام: 103] والجواب بعد تسليم كون الإبصار للاستغراق وإفادته عموم السلب لا سلب العموم وكون الإدراك هو الرؤية مطلقا لا الرؤية على وجه الإحاطة بجوانب المرئى أنه لا دلالة فيه على عموم الأوقات والأحوال. (۱) ولا وجه لما اختلف في هذه الرؤية بعد الإجماع عليها راجع بحثا في الإجماع في مقدمتي لكتاب الإجماع للحافظ النيسابوري.
And among the scriptural [proofs] is His statement the Exalted: 'No vision can grasp Him, but He grasps all vision' [al-An'am 6:103]. And the answer, after conceding that 'vision' (al-abṣār) is generic and indicates universal negation (general negation) not negation of universality, and that 'apprehension' (al-idrāk) is vision absolutely, not vision that encompasses the sides of the visible object, is that there is no indication in it of the generality of times and states. (1) And there is no basis for the disagreement about this vision after the consensus upon it; refer to the discussion on consensus in my introduction to the book al-Ijma' by al-Hafiz al-Naysaburi.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage addresses a scriptural objection: the verse 'لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ' (No vision can grasp Him). The answer is nuanced: even if we accept that 'أبصار' is generic (li al-istighrāq) and that the expression means 'universal negation' (ʿumūm al-salb) rather than 'negation of universality' (salb al-ʿumūm), and that 'idrāk' means vision in absolute terms not specifically encompassing vision, the verse does not indicate that vision is impossible at all times and states. It only denies grasp in this world or in a particular sense. The footnote adds that after consensus on the vision of Allah, there is no basis for disagreement, and references the author's work on consensus.

Key Terms
إدراك
عموم السلب
سلب العموم
استغراق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ' denies any and all vision of Allah forever.
Correction: The verse denies comprehensive grasp (encompassing vision) and does not extend to all times and states, thus allowing vision in the afterlife.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the verse 'لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ' actually deny?
A) It denies the possibility of any vision of Allah forever.
B) It denies that vision is possible in this world but not the afterlife.
C) It denies comprehensive grasp (idrāk) of Allah, not simple vision, and not for all times.
D) It denies that Allah can be seen with the physical eye.

Key Takeaway
The verse denies that anyone can encompass Allah in vision, but does not deny seeing Him entirely, especially not in the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a verse that seems to contradict a core belief you hold, do you rush to reinterpret the belief or do you patiently examine the verse's full context and scholarly consensus? This lesson teaches that a superficial reading can lead to error. Recall a time you might have misread a verse – how can you adopt the humility to seek deeper understanding before conclusions?
?
The author uses consensus (ijmā') as a decisive proof to settle the matter. In your own religious life, do you give enough weight to the collective understanding of the scholars? When a difficult issue arises, are you quick to rely on your own reading, or do you submit to the tradition of the ummah? Challenge yourself to identify one area where you trust scholarly consensus over your personal opinion.
?
The verse states 'No vision can grasp Him' – yet you affirm you will see your Lord in Paradise. Does this prospect stir genuine longing in your heart? Or has it become a mere doctrinal statement? Meditate on the reality that you will behold Allah's beauty. How can you cultivate a deeper desire for that vision starting today, so that your actions are motivated by eager anticipation rather than just duty?

The Verse Implies Possibility of Vision
Arguing that the negation in the verse presupposes possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse 'No vision can grasp Him' is used as evidence for the possibility (and actual occurrence) of seeing Allah.

Core Idea
Negation of vision only makes sense if vision is possible.

The verse 'لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ' might seem to deny the possibility of seeing Allah. However, the author argues that the very fact that Allah praises Himself for not being seen shows that seeing Him is possible. This lesson unpacks that argument and explains how the verse actually supports the Ashʿarī position on the beatific vision.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical flow: 'if it were impossible, then praise for negating it would not occur.'
2
Understand the key principle
The author uses a general logical principle: praising someone for not doing something only makes sense if that something is possible. For example, we don't praise a rock for not seeing because it's impossible for it to see.
This principle is the foundation of the argument.
3
Apply the principle to the verse
Allah says He is not grasped by vision, and this is a praise. According to the principle, this praise indicates that being seen is possible. The author adds that the reason Allah is not seen is His majesty, not impossibility.
Think of a powerful king who hides behind a veil – he can be seen but chooses not to.
4
Consider the alternative interpretation of idrāk
The author then considers another meaning: if 'idrāk' means comprehensive grasp, then the verse only negates full comprehension, not vision itself. This further supports the possibility of vision.
This shows the importance of precise terminology in kalām.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The verse actually indicates that seeing Allah is possible, and in fact occurs (in the afterlife). The negation is either a praise or limited to comprehensive grasp.
This aligns with the Ashʿarī doctrine that Allah will be seen by the believers in Paradise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يستدل بالآية على جواز الرؤية إذ لو امتنعت لما حصل التمدح بنفيها كالمعدوم لا يمدح بعدم رؤيته لامتناعها وإنما التمدح في أنه تمكن رؤيته، ولا يرى للتمنع والتعزز بحجاب الكبرياء وإن جعلنا الإدراك عبارة عن الرؤية على وجه الإحاطة بالجوانب والحدود، فدلالة الآية على جواز الرؤية، بل تحققها أظهر ولان المعنى أن الله تعالى مع كونه مرئيا لا يدرك بالأبصار، لتعاليه عن التناهي والاتصاف بالحدود والجوانب.
And it is used as evidence from the verse for the permissibility of vision, because if it were impossible, then praising by negating it would not occur, just as a non-existent thing is not praised for not being seen, because its impossibility [of being seen] is inherent. Rather, the praise is that He can be seen but is not seen out of majesty and might through the veil of grandeur. And if we take 'apprehension' (al-idrāk) as meaning vision that encompasses the sides and limits, then the indication of the verse for the permissibility of vision, indeed for its actual occurrence, is more apparent, because the meaning is that God Almighty, despite being visible, is not apprehended by sights due to His transcendence beyond finitude and being described with limits and sides.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage develops an argument from the same verse that actually supports the possibility of seeing Allah. The logic: if seeing Allah were impossible, there would be no merit in stating that He is not seen, just as no one praises a non-existent thing for not being seen. The praise implies that seeing Him is possible but He prevents it out of majesty. Furthermore, if 'idrāk' means comprehensive grasp, then the verse says that Allah is visible but not encompassed by sight—which affirms vision while denying full comprehension.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'No vision can grasp Him' proves that Allah cannot be seen at all.
Correction: The author shows that the negation in the verse is a praise, which presupposes possibility. Moreover, if 'idrāk' means comprehensive grasp, the verse only denies full comprehension, not simple vision.

Checkpoint
How does the author argue that the verse implies the possibility of seeing Allah?
A) Because the word 'idrāk' means only comprehensive vision.
B) Because praise for negating vision only makes sense if vision is possible.
C) Because the verse uses a universal negation.
D) Because the verse refers to the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
The verse that negates vision actually provides evidence for the possibility of seeing Allah, either through the logic of praise or through the distinction between idrāk and ruʾya.

?
The verse says He is not encompassed by vision. Does your prayer reflect awe of a God who is visible yet beyond comprehension, or have you reduced Him to a concept you can manage? What will you change today to worship Him as both near and majestic?
